     ```javascript
     function syncCellProps() {
       const title = document.getElementById('cellPropTitle');
       const sliders = document.getElementById('cellPropSliders');
       if (selectedSeed < 0 || selectedSeed >= seeds.length) {
         title.textContent = '— select a cell to edit its properties —';
         sliders.style.display = 'none'; return;
       }
       const s = seeds[selectedSeed];
       title.textContent = `Cell ${selectedSeed+1} · ${s.role}`;
       sliders.style.display = 'block';
       const bm = s.bondMult ?? 1, br = s.blastResist ?? 0, dm = s.densityMult ?? 1;
       document.getElementById('bondMult').value = bm;
       document.getElementById('vBondMult').textContent = bm.toFixed(2) + '×';
       document.getElementById('blastResist').value = br;
       document.getElementById('vBlastResist').textContent = Math.round(br * 100) + '%';
       document.getElementById('densityMult').value = dm;
       document.getElementById('vDensityMult').textContent = dm.toFixed(2) + '×';
     }
     ```
   - Seed creation: all `seeds.push(...)` calls add `bondMult:1, blastResist:0, densityMult:1`
   - `mirrorSeeds()` already uses spread operator `{...s}` so it copies custom props automatically ✓
   - Export: include non-default props only in seed objects
   - Import: `bondMult: s.bondMult ?? 1, blastResist: s.blastResist ?? 0, densityMult: s.densityMult ?? 1`
   - Visual ring in `drawEdit()`:
     ```javascript
     const bm = s.bondMult ?? 1;
     if (Math.abs(bm - 1) > 0.04) {
       ctx.beginPath(); ctx.arc(s.x, s.y, (hov||sel?9:6)+4, 0, TAU);
       ctx.lineWidth = clamp(Math.abs(bm-1)*2.5, 0.8, 6);
       ctx.strokeStyle = bm > 1 ? `rgba(100,220,140,0.65)` : `rgba(252,120,120,0.65)`;
       ctx.stroke();
     }
     // text labels for non-default values
     const br = s.blastResist ?? 0, dm = s.densityMult ?? 1;
     const lbls = [];
     if (Math.abs(bm-1) > 0.04) lbls.push(`B:${bm.toFixed(1)}×`);
     if (br > 0.04) lbls.push(`R:${Math.round(br*100)}%`);
     if (Math.abs(dm-1) > 0.04) lbls.push(`D:${dm.toFixed(1)}×`);
     if (lbls.length) { ctx.font='9px system-ui'; ctx.textAlign='center';
       ctx.fillStyle='rgba(190,210,255,0.6)';
       ctx.fillText(lbls.join(' '), s.x, s.y+(hov||sel?26:20)); }
     ```
   - `syncCellProps()` calls added in: mouseup seed selection, setMode(), undo(), role picker click, contextmenu after delete

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-10 15:21 UTC

Everything is wired up correctly. Here's what was added:

**UI panel** (Seeds tab, below grain slider): shows "select a cell to edit its properties" when nothing is selected; expands to show 3 sliders when a seed is clicked:
- **Bond mult** (0.1–5.0×): multiplies bond strength for all bonds adjacent to this cell. Uses geometric mean with the neighboring cell, so if cockpit=3.0 and a neighbor=1.0, that shared bond is √3 ≈ 1.73× stronger.
- **Blast resist** (0–100%): vaporization resistance, exported to JSON for the game engine.
- **Density mult** (0.1–3.0×): mass contribution multiplier, also exported.

**Visual feedback on canvas**: seeds with non-default `bondMult` show a green ring (stronger) or red ring (weaker). Any non-default property shows a small label below the seed dot like `B:2.5× R:30% D:1.5×`.

**Export**: non-default values are included in the seed JSON; defaults are omitted to keep output clean.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-10 15:39 UTC

This is worth thinking through carefully because the structure you pick now will determine how much friction there is in the editor and in the C# loading code.

---

## Asset categories

**1. Shapes** — authored in the shape editor, geometric only
```
outline, seeds[], per-cell roles + property overrides (bondMult, blastResist, densityMult)
```
These change rarely and are visual/structural, not tuning. They deserve their own files.

**2. Materials** — fracture behavior profiles referenced by name
```
rock, ice, metal, glass
  → brittleness, toughness, directionality
```

**3. Entity prefabs** — bind a shape to a material + gameplay params
```
PlayerShip
  → shape ref, material ref
  → physics (mass scale, friction, restitution)
  → health/damage model (at what structural damage % do behaviors change?)
  → visual (role-color overrides if any)

Drone, Bruiser, Mothership (boss)
  → + AI: steering weights, speed, detection radius, aggression

Asteroid variants (Standard, Gravel, Spinner, Boulder, Armored, Unstable)
  → + rotation rate, initial angular speed range
  → + spawn size scale range
```

**4. Weapon profiles**
```
Cannon     → energy, fire rate, projectile speed, spread
Shotgun    → energy per ray, ray count, cone angle
Piercing   → energy, mass, lateral impulse clamp
Grenade    → energy, fuse time, shrapnel count, shrapnel spread
```

**5. Skills**
```
Dash       → velocity spike magnitude, invincibility duration, cooldown
Turbo      → thrust multiplier, duration, cooldown
SlowMo     → time scale, player speed boost factor, duration, cooldown
```

**6. Player config**
```
thrust, rotation speed, max speed, braking drag
starting weapon, skill loadout
respawn invincibility window
```

**7. Wave definitions**
```
Wave N:
  budget, entity list with spawn weights
  spawn interval, simultaneous cap
  early-clear threshold (area remaining %)
  bonus modifiers (e.g., +spin, +armored)
```

**8. Scoring**
```
base cell score formula (area × toughness)
kill-chain multiplier steps, decay rate
wave-survival bonus
leaderboard size
```

---

## Proposed file structure

```
assets/
  shapes/
    player_ship.json      ← from shape editor
    drone.json
    bruiser.json
    mothership.json
    asteroid_standard.json
    asteroid_boulder.json
    asteroid_spinner.json
    asteroid_armored.json
    asteroid_gravel.json
    asteroid_unstable.json

  game_config.json        ← everything tuneable
```

Shapes stay separate because the editor writes them directly. `game_config.json` references shapes by filename stem.

---

## `game_config.json` sketch

```json
{
  "materials": {
    "rock":   { "brittleness": 0.7, "toughness": 8,  "directionality": 0.5 },
    "metal":  { "brittleness": 0.4, "toughness": 14, "directionality": 0.3 },
    "ice":    { "brittleness": 0.9, "toughness": 5,  "directionality": 0.6 },
    "glass":  { "brittleness": 0.95,"toughness": 3,  "directionality": 0.7 }
  },

  "weapons": {
    "cannon":   { "energy": 1200, "fireRate": 4.0, "projectileSpeed": 900 },
    "shotgun":  { "energyPerRay": 400, "rays": 7, "coneAngle": 18 },
    "piercing": { "energy": 2800, "mass": 3.0, "lateralImpulseClamp": 0.4 },
    "grenade":  { "energy": 3500, "fuseTime": 1.8, "shrapnelCount": 12, "shrapnelSpread": 360 }
  },

  "skills": {
    "dash":   { "velocitySpike": 1400, "invincibilityTime": 0.35, "cooldown": 3.0 },
    "turbo":  { "thrustMult": 3.0, "duration": 2.0, "cooldown": 8.0 },
    "slowmo": { "timeScale": 0.3, "playerSpeedBoost": 2.5, "duration": 3.0, "cooldown": 12.0 }
  },

  "player": {
    "shape": "player_ship",
    "material": "metal",
    "thrust": 420,
    "rotSpeed": 3.2,
    "maxSpeed": 680,
    "brakeDrag": 0.85,
    "startingWeapon": "cannon",
    "skills": ["dash", "turbo", "slowmo"]
  },

  "entities": {
    "drone": {
      "shape": "drone", "material": "metal",
      "speed": 220, "detectionRadius": 800,
      "steeringWeights": { "separation": 1.2, "pursuit": 0.8, "avoidance": 1.0 }
    },
    "bruiser": {
      "shape": "bruiser", "material": "metal",
      "speed": 130, "detectionRadius": 1100,
      "steeringWeights": { "separation": 0.6, "pursuit": 1.4, "avoidance": 0.5 }
    },
    "mothership": {
      "shape": "mothership", "material": "metal",
      "speed": 55, "detectionRadius": 2200
    }
  },

  "asteroids": {
    "standard": { "shape": "asteroid_standard", "material": "rock",   "sizeRange": [0.6, 1.4], "spinRange": [0.0, 1.5] },
    "gravel":   { "shape": "asteroid_gravel",   "material": "rock",   "sizeRange": [0.3, 0.8], "spinRange": [0.5, 3.0] },
    "spinner":  { "shape": "asteroid_spinner",  "material": "rock",   "sizeRange": [0.7, 1.2], "spinRange": [2.5, 5.0] },
    "boulder":  { "shape": "asteroid_boulder",  "material": "rock",   "sizeRange": [1.0, 2.0], "spinRange": [0.0, 0.8], "densityMult": 2.5 },
    "armored":  { "shape": "asteroid_armored",  "material": "metal",  "sizeRange": [0.8, 1.6], "spinRange": [0.2, 1.2] },
    "unstable": { "shape": "asteroid_unstable", "material": "glass",  "sizeRange": [0.9, 1.5], "spinRange": [1.0, 2.5] }
  },

  "waves": [
    { "wave": 1, "budget": 800,  "spawns": { "standard": 1.0 },                        "spawnInterval": 5.0, "cap": 8  },
    { "wave": 2, "budget": 1200, "spawns": { "standard": 0.7, "gravel": 0.3 },          "spawnInterval": 4.5, "cap": 10 },
    { "wave": 5, "budget": 2500, "spawns": { "standard": 0.4, "spinner": 0.3, "drone": 0.3 }, "spawnInterval": 3.5, "cap": 14 },
    { "wave": 10, "budget": 0,   "spawns": { "mothership": 1.0 },                       "spawnInterval": 0,   "cap": 1, "boss": true }
  ],

  "scoring": {
    "cellScoreBase": "area * toughness * 0.001",
    "killChainSteps": [1.0, 1.5, 2.0, 4.0],
    "killChainDecay": 3.0,
    "waveSurvivalBonus": 500,
    "leaderboardSize": 10
  }
}
```

---

## Key design decisions to nail down now

**Shapes vs. entities are separate concerns.** A shape is just geometry. An entity prefab says "use this shape, this material, and these gameplay numbers." This means you can reuse a shape with different materials (e.g., an armored asteroid uses the same shape as standard but with `"material": "metal"`).

**Wave definitions are sparse** — only define waves that introduce something new. Intermediate waves interpolate or repeat the previous pattern. Otherwise you'll have 30 nearly-identical wave entries.

**`densityMult` at the entity level vs. per-cell.** The per-cell `densityMult` in the shape editor is for structural variance (e.g., heavier core cell). The entity-level `densityMult` in asteroid config is a global size/mass modifier. Both are needed and they multiply together.

**The C# `GameConfig` library** maps 1:1 to this structure — one class per section, loaded once at startup, read-only in the game project, writable (with save) in the demo/editor project.

---

The natural next step is to build the C# `GameConfig` types and load `game_config.json` + the shape files, then hook the tuner demo up to save edits back to disk. Want to do that before the game editor UI, or is there something in this structure you want to adjust first?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-10 16:17 UTC

Good findings on directionality. Here's the full picture:

---

## Directionality — currently weapon-only, should be split

In `FractureService.cs:107`, `weapon.Directionality` is the only source — it's passed directly into the propagation kernel. `FractureProperties` has no directionality field. Your instinct is right and the fix is simple: add `CrackCleavage` (or `Directionality`) to `FractureProperties`, and in the service combine them — e.g. `effective = clamp(weapon.Dir * material.Dir * 1.5, 0, 1)` or a plain average. That way:
- **Weapon directionality** = "how focused is the impact cone" (piercing round ≈ 0.9, grenade ≈ 0.1)
- **Material directionality** = "how much does the material's grain guide the crack" (glass cleaves cleanly ≈ 0.8, rock shatters ≈ 0.5, metal tears ductilely ≈ 0.2)

This is a one-line engine change when we're ready.

---

## Revised structure, addressing all your feedback

### 1. Shapes — add procedural asteroid descriptor

Authored shapes stay as `.json` files. Procedural asteroids use a descriptor in `game_config.json` instead of a shape file reference — they share the same slot but with a `procedural` block instead of `shape`:

```json
"asteroid_standard": {
  "procedural": {
    "baseRadius": 80,
    "vertexCount": [10, 16],
    "roughness": 0.22,
    "noiseFrequency": 3,
    "concavityBias": 0.05,
    "seedCount": [6, 10],
    "seedClusterCenter": 0.3
  },
  "material": "rock",
  "sizeRange": [0.6, 1.4],
  "spinRange": [0.0, 1.5]
}
```

`roughness` = noise amplitude as fraction of base radius. `seedClusterCenter` biases seeds toward the centroid (gives boulders a dense core). Authored shapes (drone, mothership) use `"shape": "drone"` as before — same structure, different key. The loader checks for `shape` first, falls back to `procedural`.

---

### 4. Weapons — fix shotgun, add TTL

```json
"weapons": {
  "cannon": {
    "energy": 1200, "fireRate": 4.0,
    "projectileSpeed": 900, "timeToLive": 2.5
  },
  "shotgun": {
    "energyPerRay": 400, "rays": 7, "coneAngle": 18,
    "projectileSpeed": 750, "timeToLive": 1.2
  },
  "piercing": {
    "energy": 2800, "mass": 3.0, "lateralImpulseClamp": 0.4,
    "projectileSpeed": 1100, "timeToLive": 3.0
  },
  "grenade": {
    "energy": 3500, "fuseTime": 1.8,
    "shrapnelCount": 12, "shrapnelSpread": 360,
    "projectileSpeed": 320, "timeToLive": 4.0
  }
}
```

`timeToLive` is in seconds and is independent of distance — the projectile despawns at expiry regardless. If we later want a max-range feel, distance-to-TTL is just `speed × timeToLive`.

---

### 6. Player — add respawn

```json
"player": {
  "shape": "player_ship", "material": "metal",
  "thrust": 420, "rotSpeed": 3.2, "maxSpeed": 680, "brakeDrag": 0.85,
  "startingWeapon": "cannon",
  "skills": ["dash", "turbo", "slowmo"],
  "respawn": {
    "delay": 2.5,
    "invincibilityTime": 3.0,
    "penalty": "loseMultiplier"
  }
}
```

`penalty` is a string tag — options like `"none"`, `"loseMultiplier"`, `"loseScore500"` — interpreted by game code. Keeps it data-driven for tuning.

---

### 7. Waves — reworked

Two wave types: `"budget"` and `"explicit"`. Global cell cap lives at the top level. Spawn pattern and modifiers on every wave.

```json
"maxLiveCells": 600,

"waves": [
  {
    "wave": 1,
    "type": "budget",
    "budget": 800,
    "spawns": { "asteroid_standard": 1.0 },
    "spawnPattern": "burst",
    "modifiers": []
  },
  {
    "wave": 3,
    "type": "budget",
    "budget": 1400,
    "spawns": { "asteroid_standard": 0.6, "asteroid_gravel": 0.4 },
    "spawnPattern": "rapid",
    "rapidInterval": 0.4,
    "modifiers": []
  },
  {
    "wave": 5,
    "type": "explicit",
    "asteroids": [
      { "type": "asteroid_boulder", "count": 2, "spawnDelay": 0.0 },
      { "type": "asteroid_spinner", "count": 4, "spawnDelay": 0.8 },
      { "type": "asteroid_gravel",  "count": 8, "spawnDelay": 1.6 }
    ],
    "spawnPattern": "staggered",
    "modifiers": ["high_spin"]
  },
  {
    "wave": 10,
    "type": "explicit",
    "asteroids": [
      { "type": "mothership", "count": 1, "spawnDelay": 0.0 }
    ],
    "spawnPattern": "burst",
    "modifiers": [],
    "boss": true
  }
]
```

`spawnPattern`: `"burst"` = all at once, `"rapid"` = one every `rapidInterval` seconds, `"staggered"` = one every 0.5–1.5s (randomized). `"budget"` waves auto-calculate how many entities to spawn based on their cell counts and `maxLiveCells`.

---

## Extensibility for textures/sprites/animations

The answer is yes — the structure handles it cleanly with a `visual` block per entity that's currently empty. Physics/fracture never touches it. When you add visuals:

```json
"drone": {
  "shape": "drone", "material": "metal",
  "speed": 220,
  ...
  "visual": {
    "theme": "alien_blue",
    "roleTints": { "cannon": "#ff4040", "cockpit": "#ffe060" },
    "engineTrail": "blue_flame",
    "deathEffect": "explosion_medium"
  }
}
```

Animations for a cell-based body won't be sprite sheets — the cells are dynamic polygons. What makes sense is:
- **Role-based glow/pulse** (cockpit pulses, engines trail particles) — driven by role tags already in the shape
- **Screen effects** (slowmo vignette, hit flash) — global, defined separately
- **Particle systems** referenced by name (resolved at load time)

A separate `effects.json` for particle/shader definitions keeps them decoupled from gameplay tuning. `game_config.json` references effect names; `effects.json` defines the emitter parameters. That boundary will be stable regardless of how complex the visual side gets.

---

The one question worth resolving now: **do asteroids that get split by fracture spawn wave-budget chunks, or are child fragments free/unbudgeted?** That determines whether `maxLiveCells` needs to account for fracture debris, or just live "whole" asteroids.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-11 09:44 UTC

Good call — this is exactly the kind of per-cell variance that makes the materials feel distinct. A boulder should resist cracking from inside out, an armored asteroid should have a tough shell, an unstable one should have random weak pockets.

I'll add a `CellPropertyDistribution` type and wire it into `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` for all three properties, then fill in meaningful distributions for each asteroid variant.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-11 09:44 UTC

Now update `game_config.json` with meaningful distributions for the variants that need them. Standard and gravel stay null (uniform); the interesting ones are boulder, armored, spinner, and unstable:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-11 09:45 UTC

Good. Here's what the distributions mean for each variant:

**Spinner** — `bondMult` radial gradient, *centerValue 0.6 → surfaceValue 1.4, exponent 2.0*. The outer cells hold together tightly (they resist the centrifugal force), but the core is pre-weakened — hit a spinner dead center and it peels apart from the inside.

**Boulder** — `bondMult` strong center (3.0) fading out (0.7), `densityMult` same gradient (2.0 → 0.9). Dense, tough core; crumbly exterior chips off first, making it take many hits to crack the heart. The global `densityMult: 2.5` stacks on top of the per-cell gradient.

**Armored** — `bondMult` inverted gradient (0.7 → 3.5, exponent 3.0 = very steep, almost a shell), `blastResist` same (0.0 → 0.8, exponent 4.0 = nearly all the resistance lives at the very edge). Weapons bounce off the surface; you need to punch through or flank it.

**Unstable** — both `bondMult` and `blastResist` use `noiseClusters`. Random pockets of strongly bonded material mixed with fragile zones — fractures unpredictably, sometimes releasing intact chunks, sometimes vaporizing a pocket. The noise on `blastResist` means even a grenade won't destroy it uniformly.

The generator just needs to evaluate `CellPropertyDistribution.Evaluate(r)` per cell, where `r` is the normalised radial position. That method can live in the GameConfig library as a simple helper when we implement the procedural generator.

Perfect. What are the next steps?

     - Added `syncCellProps()` function:
       ```javascript
       function syncCellProps() {
         const title = document.getElementById('cellPropTitle');
         const sliders = document.getElementById('cellPropSliders');
         if (!title) return;
         if (selectedSeed < 0 || selectedSeed >= seeds.length) {
           title.textContent = '— select a cell to edit its properties —';
           sliders.style.display = 'none'; return;
         }
         const s = seeds[selectedSeed];
         title.textContent = `Cell ${selectedSeed+1} · ${s.role}`;
         sliders.style.display = 'block';
         const bm = s.bondMult ?? 1, br = s.blastResist ?? 0, dm = s.densityMult ?? 1;
         document.getElementById('bondMult').value = bm;
         document.getElementById('vBondMult').textContent = bm.toFixed(2) + '×';
         document.getElementById('blastResist').value = br;
         document.getElementById('vBlastResist').textContent = Math.round(br * 100) + '%';
         document.getElementById('densityMult').value = dm;
         document.getElementById('vDensityMult').textContent = dm.toFixed(2) + '×';
       }
       ```
     - `buildVoronoi()`: cells now include `bondMult:s.bondMult??1, blastResist:s.blastResist??0, densityMult:s.densityMult??1`
     - `rebuildBonds()`: `const bm=Math.sqrt((cells[i].bondMult??1)*(cells[j].bondMult??1));` geometric mean applied to bond strength
     - Visual ring on seeds: green ring (bm>1) or red ring (bm<1), text labels B:/R:/D:
     - `mirrorSeeds()` uses `{...s, x:...}` spread for both axes
     - Export omits default values; import uses `?? default` fallback
     - `syncCellProps()` called in: mouseup seed select, setMode(), undo(), role picker click, contextmenu delete

   - **`/home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Engine/Components/FractureProperties.cs`**
     - Added `CrackDirectionality` field with XML doc comment

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-11 10:31 UTC

Good timing to address all three before writing more code — these affect core architecture.

---

**1. Game Editor / Config-Driven Workflow**

Yes, the game reads everything from `GameConfig`: player thrust, weapon fire rate/energy, material toughness/brittleness, etc. — all via `ConfigExtensions`. The demo currently uses its own hardcoded `Tuner` params and ignores the config entirely.

The right move is to make the demo the editor. The workflow becomes:

```
Browser shape editor  →  Assets/shapes/*.json
Demo (as game editor) →  Assets/game_config.json
         ↓
    Real game loads both at startup
```

Concretely, the demo would:
- Load `game_config.json` at startup (same `GameConfigLoader.Load`)
- Expose each material/weapon/asteroid variant as a **selectable object** in the panel (cycle with Tab/M)
- Map the selected object's fields to Tuner sliders (binding, not copy)
- Press **S** to save back to `game_config.json`
- Press **1–6** to instantly spawn that asteroid variant; press **W/E** to cycle active weapon for testing

The Tuner panel already handles live editing. The new part is the object-selector and the save-back. This is maybe 2–3 sessions of work but pays off immediately — every subsequent content session happens in the editor without touching code.

One strong suggestion: keep the Tuner's flat slider list but organize it into named **sections** (e.g. `[rock material]`, `[cannon weapon]`, `[boulder asteroid]`). Switching the selected object swaps the section, not the whole UI. This avoids building a real UI system.

---

**2. Wave System — Organic Flow**

The current design (pause + full reset) is wrong. The corrected model:

- `PlayingState` owns the full wave progression internally — no `WaveCompleteState` screen pause for normal waves
- At wave-end (timer OR all wave-spawned enemies dead), `PlayingState` spawns the next wave's additions directly, shows a brief HUD banner ("WAVE 3 INCOMING"), continues running
- New spawns = `min(waveBudget, maxLiveCells - currentLiveCells)`
- If `currentLiveCells >= maxLiveCells`, nothing new spawns — the player is already overwhelmed
- Only the boss wave completion (wave 10 cleared) → transition to `GameOverState(won)`

WaveDefinition needs one new field: `Duration` (seconds until wave ends regardless of clear state). The spawn budget already exists; it just becomes "additive cells" not "total cells."

This makes `WaveCompleteState` dead code for normal play — can repurpose it as a short overlay or delete it.

---

**3. World Size — 5760×5760 with Force Field**

This requires three things that don't exist yet:

**Camera** — smooth-follow transform, world→screen projection. Every render call needs `worldPos - cameraPos` offset. The camera should lag slightly behind the player (feels better than locked-on).

**Viewport culling** — at 5760² the entity count won't be huge, but we should skip rendering bodies whose AABB doesn't intersect the viewport. The collision spatial grid already handles physics correctly at any scale.

**Border force field** — apply a soft repulsive force when an entity's position enters the danger band (e.g. last 200px from any edge). Force = `k × (overlap / bandWidth)²`, pointing inward. This applies to both player and asteroids; aliens could also be attracted back to center. Visual: a faint color-shifting glow along the edges.

---

**What I'd tackle in order:**

1. **Camera + world size** — foundational, everything else needs it
2. **Wave redesign** — integrate into `PlayingState` properly before the editor
3. **Demo → game editor** — biggest workflow impact, worthwhile once the game loop is stable

Want me to start with the camera + world expansion, or jump to the editor first?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-11 12:37 UTC

Good plan overall. Honest feedback before we commit to an approach:

---

**What's solid:**

Points 3 and 4 are exactly right. Per-file assets (not overwriting one big config) and a hot-assembling simulator are how professional game editors work. This should absolutely drive the architecture.

---

**Where I'd push back or add nuance:**

**On point 1 (mouse-clickable UI):** This is a real mini-project. SDL + SkiaSharp means we have a CPU canvas with no UI framework. Options are:

- **Minimal immediate-mode GUI over SkiaSharp** — ~400 lines: hit-testing, buttons, sliders, collapsible panels. Everything rendered via `IRenderer`. Fits our architecture, stays CPU-side, matches the rendering pipeline exactly.
- **Dear ImGui (ImGui.NET)** — the industry standard for game editors. Problem: it expects an OpenGL or DX renderer, and we're using a CPU SkiaSharp canvas. Integration is awkward and would likely require switching the rendering backend.

I'd go with the first option. It's less impressive on paper but ships faster and stays coherent with the engine.

**On point 2 (reflection-based auto-UI):** Attractive but deceptive. The issue is that `float Toughness` in code carries no metadata — no min, no max, no step size, no description. Pure reflection gives you labels and raw numbers but not a usable editor. You'll end up annotating every field anyway:

```csharp
[Range(0.1f, 20f), Description("Crack resistance")]
public float Toughness { get; set; }
```

At which point you've done almost as much work as explicit binding. My suggestion: a **fluent `EditorDef<T>`** per config class:

```csharp
EditorDef.For<MaterialConfig>()
    .Slider(m => m.Toughness,    0.1f, 20f, "Crack resistance")
    .Slider(m => m.Brittleness,  0f,   5f,  "Propagation aggressiveness")
    .Slider(m => m.GrainArea,    10f,  800f, "Avg cell area")
    // ...
```

The renderer iterates any `EditorDef<T>` with the same 50 lines of code. Adding a new field = one line in the def. Nested types get their own `EditorDef` and compose. This is explicit but compact, and it stays in sync because it's code, not generated.

---

**What I'd add:**

- **Undo within a session** — when dragging a slider live, ctrl+Z to step back. Without this you'll inevitably ruin a good tuning and have no way back. A 30-step per-session history per asset is straightforward.
- **A/B comparison** — hold a snapshot of the current asset and toggle between it and your live edits. Invaluable when tuning fracture feel.
- **Shape preview in the editor** — when you select an asteroid config in the simulator, it shows the shape rendered (without physics) so you know what you're spawning.

---

**On the asset file structure:**

The current `game_config.json` puts everything in one dictionary. The proposed per-file approach means rethinking the layout:

```
Assets/
  materials/    rock.json, ice.json, metal.json, glass.json
  weapons/      cannon.json, shotgun.json, ...
  asteroids/    boulder.json, spinner.json, ...
  waves/        wave_01.json, wave_02.json, ...
  shapes/       (already exists)
  player.json
  game_config.json  ← becomes a manifest: lists which files to load + global params (maxLiveCells, scoring)
```

The loader scans each subdirectory, keys by filename stem. `game_config.json` holds only the non-asset globals. This is a breaking change to the current structure but it's the right one to make before we go deep on content.

---

**Suggested plan:**

1. Restructure `Assets/` to subdirectories + update `GameConfigLoader` (one session)
2. Build the minimal immediate-mode UI layer over SkiaSharp (one session)
3. Wire `EditorDef<T>` definitions per config class and render them in the demo panel (one-two sessions)
4. Add Load/Save As file dialogs + undo (one session)
5. Simulator mode: asset picker + spawn controls (one session)

That's ~5 focused sessions to have a fully functional editor. Should we start with the `Assets/` restructure since everything downstream depends on it?

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-11 12:42 UTC

Is it worth it to implement a GPU renderer backend? What's the difference between CPU and GPU renderers, I would guess the latter is much faster and should be desirable in a game anyway, if so we should consider implementing it right now

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-11 12:43 UTC

Honest answer: it depends on what's actually slow, and for this game the situation is more nuanced than "GPU is always better."

---

**What the current pipeline does:**

Skia draws polygons/lines into a CPU bitmap → every frame, that bitmap (~8MB at 1920×1080) is copied to an SDL texture → SDL blits it to the display. The rendering is fully software-rasterized on CPU cores.

**What a GPU pipeline does:**

Draw calls become commands in a buffer sent to the GPU. The GPU rasterizes polygons, runs fragment shaders, composites — all in hardware, in parallel, without touching CPU RAM for pixel data.

---

**Does it matter for this game?**

The bottleneck in this game is almost certainly **not** rendering. It's the fracture simulation: bond-graph traversal, crack front propagation, Voronoi cell contact solving. That's CPU work and can't move to the GPU without a major rewrite of the physics.

For rendering: at peak load you have maybe 600 live cells × (fill + edge lines) + particles + HUD. SkiaSharp's software renderer handles ~200–500 filled convex polygons in under 5ms on a modern CPU. You'll be fine at 120fps unless you push cell counts well above 600 or add expensive effects.

The one real cost is the **pixel copy**: at 120fps, copying 8MB per frame is ~1 GB/s of memory bandwidth. Not catastrophic but measurable.

---

**The right move: SkiaSharp's own GPU backend**

Skia has a native GPU backend (`GRContext` / OpenGL or Vulkan). The API is identical — same `SKCanvas`, same draw calls — but rasterization happens on the GPU and there's no pixel copy. You'd change maybe 60 lines in `SdlGameWindow.cs` and `SkiaRenderer.cs`:

```
SDL window + OpenGL context
    → GRContext.CreateGL()
    → SKSurface.Create(grContext, ...)
    → same SKCanvas, same IRenderer, same game code
    → SwapBuffers() instead of texture copy
```

Everything above `IRenderer` stays untouched. This is half a day's work, contained to the platform layer.

**Don't** build a custom OpenGL renderer (custom shaders, VBO batching, etc.). That's weeks of work for a visual style — filled polygons and lines — that Skia already handles well. The only scenario where you'd need it is if you want effects that Skia can't do cheaply (e.g., per-cell heat distortion shaders, GPU particle simulation). Those aren't in scope.

---

**Verdict:**

Yes, switch to SkiaSharp GPU now. The change is:
- Contained to `Platform/Sdl/SdlGameWindow.cs` (OpenGL context setup + surface creation)
- No effect on `IRenderer` or any game code
- Eliminates the pixel-copy cost
- Makes the editor fast (lots of UI elements will be rendered)
- Should be done before building the editor, not after

It's the right time — doing it later means retesting everything that currently works.

Want me to implement it? The main dependency is whether `Silk.NET.SDL` (which you're already using) exposes `SDL_GL_CreateContext`, which it does. We'd add `SkiaSharp.Views.Desktop` or just use `GRGlInterface.CreateOpenGl` directly — no new heavy dependencies.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-11 13:05 UTC

Done. Here's what changed and why:

**What was replaced:**
- `SKBitmap` + `SKCanvas` (CPU bitmap, 8MB per frame) → `SKSurface` on the default OpenGL framebuffer
- `SDL_CreateRenderer` + `SDL_CreateTexture` + `SDL_UpdateTexture` + `SDL_RenderCopy` → `SDL_GL_CreateContext` + `SDL_GL_SwapWindow`
- ~74 MB/s pixel copy (at 120 fps) → GPU rasterisation, zero copy

**The non-obvious issue:** `GRGlInterface.CreateOpenGl()` uses `glXGetProcAddressARB` from `libGL.so.1` (GLX, X11). On this Wayland system, SDL creates the OpenGL context via EGL, so GLX proc addresses are invalid and crash immediately. Fixed by loading `eglGetProcAddress` from `libEGL.so.1` and routing Skia's proc getter through it. The GLX path is still there as a fallback for X11-only setups.

**`IGameWindow` interface** is now correctly GPU-agnostic: `Renderer` property + `Present()`, no CPU pixel pointer. All other code above the platform layer is unchanged — `IRenderer` API is identical whether the canvas is CPU or GPU-backed.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-11 13:11 UTC

Good. Here's the concrete execution plan based on what we agreed:

---

**Phase 1 — ImGui-lite UI layer** (`Engine/Ui/Ui.cs`, ~500 lines)

An immediate-mode UI built on top of `IRenderer` + `InputSystem`. Every frame you call widget methods; they draw and return interaction state. Stateful minimum: which slider is being dragged, which list item is selected, scroll position per panel.

Core widgets needed: `BeginPanel/EndPanel`, `Button`, `Slider` (horizontal drag, label + track + value), `SliderInt`, `Label`, `Separator`, `Header` (collapsible section), `Tabs`, `SelectableList`. IDs are hashed from the label string — sufficient since labels are unique per panel.

---

**Phase 2 — EditorDef binding layer** (`Engine/Ui/EditorDef.cs` + `ConfigEditorDefs.cs`, ~250 lines)

```csharp
EditorDef.For<MaterialConfig>()
    .Slider(m => m.Toughness,    0.1f, 20f)
    .Slider(m => m.Brittleness,  0f,   5f)
    ...
```

Expression trees compiled once at startup to typed getter/setter pairs. `def.Draw(ui, ref config)` returns `true` if any value changed. One `EditorDef` per config class, all in `ConfigEditorDefs.cs`.

---

**Phase 3 — Demo → Editor** (restructure `Program.cs` + `DemoSession`)

Layout: tab bar across top `[Simulate | Materials | Weapons | Asteroids | Waves | Player]`, left sidebar (asset list for the active tab, 200px), right panel (param sliders for the selected asset, 300px), simulation viewport fills the rest.

Replaces the existing keyboard `Tuner` and its `Config` class entirely. The demo loads `game_config.json` via `GameConfigLoader`, edits live in memory, and has:
- **Load / Save As** per asset: reads/writes individual entries as standalone JSON files under `Assets/materials/`, `Assets/weapons/`, etc.
- **Revert** button: restores the in-memory entry from its last saved state (snapshot on load + on save)
- **A/B**: one button that swaps between a held snapshot and the live edit, so you can hear/see the difference

---

**Phase 4 — Simulate mode**

The tab named "Simulate" shows the full world viewport. Controls: asteroid type selector, spawn button, weapon selector, respawn all. Params are live — slider changes take effect on the next spawn or immediately for live bodies (the existing `TunableApplySystem` approach). Wave scripting is separate, lower priority.

---

**One open question before we start:** the Save As per asset currently requires no change to the loader (game still reads the big `game_config.json`). Individual files are a separate export feature. I'd keep it that way rather than restructuring the directory layout now. Agree?

If yes, we start with Phase 1 — the UI layer. Want me to begin?

     ```csharp
     }
     ```

     - Removed: `SdlRenderer*`, `Texture*`, `SKBitmap`, `SKCanvas`
     - Added: `void* _glContext`, `GRContext _grContext`, `SKSurface _surface`
     - Constructor GL init sequence:
       ```csharp
       _sdl.GLSetAttribute(GLattr.ContextMajorVersion, 3);
       _sdl.GLSetAttribute(GLattr.ContextMinorVersion, 3);
       _sdl.GLSetAttribute(GLattr.ContextProfileMask, (int)GLprofile.Core);
       _sdl.GLSetAttribute(GLattr.StencilSize, 8);
       _sdl.GLSetAttribute(GLattr.Doublebuffer, 1);
       // CreateWindow with WindowFlags.Opengl
       // GLCreateContext → GLMakeCurrent → GLSetSwapInterval(0)
       var glInterface = CreateGlInterface() ?? throw ...;
       _grContext = GRContext.CreateGl(glInterface) ?? throw ...;
       var fbInfo = new GRGlFramebufferInfo(0, 0x8058); // GL_RGBA8
       var rt = new GRBackendRenderTarget(width, height, 0, 8, fbInfo);
       _surface = SKSurface.Create(_grContext, rt, GRSurfaceOrigin.BottomLeft, SKColorType.Rgba8888) ?? throw ...;
       _skiaRenderer = new SkiaRenderer(_surface.Canvas);
       ```
     - `Present()`: `_surface.Canvas.Flush(); _grContext.Flush(); _sdl.GLSwapWindow(_window);`
     - Key static method:
       ```csharp
       private static GRGlInterface? CreateGlInterface()
       {
           // EGL — Wayland and modern X11 with EGL.
           if (NativeLibrary.TryLoad("libEGL.so.1", out var egl) &&
               NativeLibrary.TryGetExport(egl, "eglGetProcAddress", out var eglFn))
           {
               var getter = Marshal.GetDelegateForFunctionPointer<ProcGetter>(eglFn);
               var iface  = GRGlInterface.Create(name => getter(name));
               if (iface?.Validate() == true) return iface;
           }
           // GLX — classic X11.
           if (NativeLibrary.TryLoad("libGL.so.1", out var gl) &&
               NativeLibrary.TryGetExport(gl, "glXGetProcAddressARB", out var glxFn))
           {
               var getter = Marshal.GetDelegateForFunctionPointer<ProcGetter>(glxFn);
               var iface  = GRGlInterface.Create(name => getter(name));
               if (iface?.Validate() == true) return iface;
           }
           return null;
       }

       [UnmanagedFunctionPointer(CallingConvention.Cdecl)]
       private delegate IntPtr ProcGetter([MarshalAs(UnmanagedType.LPStr)] string name);
       ```
     - `Dispose()` order: skiaRenderer → surface → grContext → GLDeleteContext → DestroyWindow → Quit

   - **`GameEngine/Platform/Sdl/SkiaRenderer.cs`** - NO CHANGES (SKCanvas API identical whether CPU or GPU backed)

   - **`GRGlFramebufferInfo` doesn't have named parameters**:
     - Changed `new GRGlFramebufferInfo(framebuffer: 0, format: 0x8058)` to positional `new GRGlFramebufferInfo(0, 0x8058)`

   - **Deprecated GL enum names in Silk.NET.SDL 2.21.0**:
     - `GLattr.GLContextMajorVersion` → `GLattr.ContextMajorVersion`
     - `GLattr.GLContextMinorVersion` → `GLattr.ContextMinorVersion`  
     - `GLattr.GLContextProfileMask` → `GLattr.ContextProfileMask`
     - `GLprofile.GLContextProfileCore` → `GLprofile.Core`
     - `GLattr.GLStencilSize` → `GLattr.StencilSize`
     - `GLattr.GLDoublebuffer` → `GLattr.Doublebuffer`

   - **SIGSEGV (exit 139) on startup**:
     - Root cause: SDL2 on Wayland creates OpenGL context via EGL. `GRGlInterface.CreateOpenGl()` internally uses GLX (`glXGetProcAddressARB` from `libGL.so.1`). Calling GLX proc addresses on an EGL context causes immediate SIGSEGV inside libSkiaSharp.so.
     - Fixed by: loading `eglGetProcAddress` from `libEGL.so.1` via `NativeLibrary.TryLoad` + `Marshal.GetDelegateForFunctionPointer`, then routing through `GRGlInterface.Create(proc)`. GLX fallback for X11-only systems.
     - Verified: exit code 124 (timeout killed) not 139 (crash)

   - **`GRGlInterface.CreateOpenGl()` (no-args) doesn't exist in SkiaSharp 2.88.7**:
     - Only `CreateOpenGl(GRGlGetProcedureAddressDelegate)` exists (requires proc getter)
     - Fixed GLX fallback to explicitly load `glXGetProcAddressARB` from `libGL.so.1` via NativeLibrary

   - **GPU backend**: The core challenge was the EGL vs GLX mismatch on Wayland. Diagnosed by adding Console.Error.WriteLines at each init step, confirming crash was inside `GRGlInterface.Create/CreateOpenGl`. Confirmed EGL availability via a small C test program (`eglGetProcAddress` at non-null address). Solution: use `NativeLibrary.TryLoad("libEGL.so.1")` to get the EGL proc getter and pass it to Skia. The solution is also portable: falls back to GLX for X11-only systems.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - C# game engine with ECS architecture (World, Entity, ISystem, EventBus)
   - Cell/bond-graph Voronoi fracture model with multi-frame crack propagation
   - GameConfig (pure data library): JSON source of truth loaded at startup via `GameConfigLoader`
   - System.Text.Json with camelCase naming policy, `DefaultIgnoreCondition.WhenWritingNull`
   - GPU rendering: SkiaSharp GRContext (OpenGL via EGL on Wayland, GLX fallback)
   - `r.End()` only calls `canvas.Flush()` (doesn't swap) — so editor draw calls appended AFTER `renderer.Draw()` are submitted in `window.Present()`'s final flush (pure overlay pattern)
   - Immediate-mode UI: stateful minimum (_activeId for drag, _focusedInputId for text), widgets draw and return interaction state
   - EditorDef<T>: expression-tree-compiled getter/setter pairs for type-safe data binding
   - `InputSystem.SuppressMouseLeft`: set before game simulation runs (using previous frame's geometry check, no lag since check is pure geometry)
   - `InputSystem.IsMouseLeftRaw`: for UI layer to always receive clicks regardless of suppression
   - SDL `EventType.Textinput` → `TextInputEvent.Text` is `<Text>e__FixedBuffer`, accessed via `Marshal.PtrToStringUTF8((IntPtr)(&ev.Text.Text))`

3. Files and Code Sections:

   - **`GameEngine/Engine/Ui/Ui.cs`** (created, ~450 lines)
     - Immediate-mode UI context class
     - Dark game-editor theme (15,16,22 background; 75,135,235 accent blue)
     - Mouse edge-detection self-contained (compares prev/current frame `IsMouseLeftRaw`)
     - FNV-1a hashed widget IDs: `ulong h = 14695981039346656037UL; h ^= c; h *= 1099511628211UL`
     - BeginRow/EndRow for horizontal button strips: calculates `_rowItemW = (pw - 2*Pad - gap*(count-1)) / count`
     - Slider: click-or-drag on track, thumb knob at fill position, `AutoFmt` selects decimal precision
     - TextInput widget (added during feedback phase):
       ```csharp
       public bool TextInput(string id, ref string value, bool autoFocus = false, float? width = null)
       // Returns true when Enter committed. Escape cancels. autoFocus grabs focus if nothing else focused.
       ```
     - New state fields: `_textInput`, `_backspace`, `_enterKey`, `_escapeKey`, `_focusedInputId`, `_inputBuffer`, `_cursorPos`
     - `IsTextInputActive => _focusedInputId != 0`
     - `BeginFrame` now uses `input.IsMouseLeftRaw` (not `input.IsMouseLeft`) so UI always gets raw clicks

   - **`GameEngine/Engine/Ui/EditorDef.cs`** (created)
     - `public sealed class EditorDef<T> where T : class`
     - Expression-tree compilation via `Bind<TV>(Expression<Func<T, TV>>)`:
       ```csharp
       var get = expr.Compile();
       var memberExpr = (MemberExpression)expr.Body;
       var tParam = Expression.Parameter(typeof(T));
       var vParam = Expression.Parameter(typeof(TV));
       var prop = Expression.MakeMemberAccess(tParam, memberExpr.Member);
       var assign = Expression.Assign(prop, vParam);
       var set = Expression.Lambda<Action<T, TV>>(assign, tParam, vParam).Compile();
       ```
     - Explicit lambda overloads for non-simple properties (array elements):
       ```csharp
       public EditorDef<T> Slider(string label, Func<T, float> getter, Action<T, float> setter, float min, float max, string? fmt = null)
       public EditorDef<T> SliderInt(string label, Func<T, int> getter, Action<T, int> setter, int min, int max)
       ```
     - `Draw(T obj, Ui ui)` iterates `List<Func<T, Ui, bool>>` entries

   - **`GameEngine/Demos/AsteroidDemo/ConfigEditorDefs.cs`** (created)
     - `namespace AsteroidDemo`, `static class ConfigEditorDefs`
     - `Material`: 12 float sliders covering all MaterialConfig properties

     - `ProceduralShape`: 5 float sliders + 4 int array sliders via explicit lambdas:

     - `Player`: 4 sliders (Thrust, RotSpeed, MaxSpeed, BrakeDrag)

     - Added EventType.Textinput handling:
       ```csharp
       case EventType.Textinput:
           string textChars;
           unsafe { textChars = Marshal.PtrToStringUTF8((IntPtr)(&ev.Text.Text)) ?? ""; }
           if (textChars.Length > 0) TextInput?.Invoke(textChars);
           break;
       ```
     - Note: `TextInputEvent.Text` is `Silk.NET.SDL.TextInputEvent+<Text>e__FixedBuffer` (confirmed via reflection), accessed by taking address of the struct

4. Errors and Fixes:
   - **`Editor` type not found (CS0246)**: Top-level statements in Program.cs are in global namespace; Editor is in `namespace AsteroidDemo`. Fix: added `using AsteroidDemo;` to Program.cs.
   - **`TextInputEvent.Text` field type**: Confirmed via reflection as `Silk.NET.SDL.TextInputEvent+<Text>e__FixedBuffer` — accessed by taking the address and casting: `Marshal.PtrToStringUTF8((IntPtr)(&ev.Text.Text))`
   - **Ui.BeginFrame used `IsMouseLeft` instead of `IsMouseLeftRaw`**: When `SuppressMouseLeft` is set to block game shooting, it would also block UI widgets. Fixed by changing `BeginFrame` to use `input.IsMouseLeftRaw`.

5. Problem Solving:
   - **Click suppression architecture**: Chose geometry-based approach (`IsMouseOverPanel(mouse, screenW)`) rather than drawing-state-based (no 1-frame lag). The check is pure math: `mouse.Y < TabH || (tab!=0 && (mouse.X < LeftW || mouse.X > W - RightW))`.
   - **Overlay rendering**: After `r.End()` (which calls `canvas.Flush()`), drawing more Skia commands to the same canvas is valid — they're submitted in `window.Present()`'s final flush+swap. No screen clear needed.
   - **Array element bindings in EditorDef**: Expression trees can't assign to array elements (`p.VertexCount[0]`). Solved by adding explicit `Func<T,TV> getter, Action<T,TV> setter` overloads.
   - **Weapon type-specific fields**: WeaponConfig has nullable shotgun/grenade/piercing fields. Will be handled in Editor.cs `DrawParamEditor` with Enable/Remove toggle buttons per nullable section, not in EditorDef.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-11 15:45 UTC

Clean build. Here's what changed:

**Text input bug fixed:**
- Removed the SDL `Textinput` event handler entirely (it was reading from the event union via pointer arithmetic, producing unreliable bytes on Linux)
- Now derives printable chars directly from `SDL_KEYDOWN` sym codes: a–z, 0–9, `_`, `-`, space — sufficient for asset names and includes key repeat automatically

**Keyboard suppression:**
- Added `SuppressKeyboard` to `InputSystem`; `IsHeld` / `IsPressed` return false when active, except `Back`, `Enter`, `Escape` always pass through (needed by the text widget)
- Program.cs sets `input.SuppressKeyboard = editor.IsTextInputActive` — so WASD/R/M etc. don't reach game systems while typing a name

**Escape-cancel fixed:**
- After `TextInput()` returns false, if `!_ui.IsTextInputActive` the widget was escaped/defocused → `_editingName` and `_renameIsNew` are cleared, preventing the auto-focus loop

**Skills in Player tab:**
- Left panel shows "Player" selectable + all `config.Skills` keys
- Right panel shows base player params (shape/material/Thrust/RotSpeed/MaxSpeed/BrakeDrag) or a selected skill's Cooldown/Duration + type-specific nullable sections (Dash, Turbo, Slow-Mo) with Enable/Remove toggles

**Player movement:**
- `SpawnPlayer`: `LinearDrag = 0`, `AngularDrag = 0` — physics drag no longer touches the player
- `TunableApplySystem`: skips entities with `PlayerTag`
- `PlayerControlSystem`: instant velocity impulse (130 px/s) on first key press → sustained acceleration toward max speed (650 px/s) at 2200 px/s² → exponential brake at 6 s⁻¹ when no key held (≈0.5s to stop)
- New tunables under `-- PLAYER --`: Impulse, Accel rate, Max speed, Brake

1. Primary Request and Intent:

The project is "Asteroids on Steroids" — a single-player arcade game built on a C# 2D physics/destruction engine. This session was a continuation implementing the game editor in phases:

- **Previously completed**: Phase 1 (ImGui-lite UI layer), Phase 2 (EditorDef binding layer), Phase 3 (Demo → Game Editor transformation). Infrastructure changes (InputSystem text support, SdlGameWindow TextInput event, Ui.TextInput widget, SuppressMouseLeft) were also done.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
   - C# game engine with ECS architecture (World, Entity, ISystem, EventBus)
   - Cell/bond-graph Voronoi fracture model with multi-frame crack propagation
   - GameConfig (pure data library): JSON source of truth loaded via `GameConfigLoader` from `Assets/game_config.json`
   - System.Text.Json with camelCase naming policy, `DefaultIgnoreCondition.WhenWritingNull`
   - GPU rendering: SkiaSharp GRContext (OpenGL via EGL on Wayland / GLX fallback)
   - Immediate-mode UI: `Ui.cs` class — stateful widgets with FNV-1a hashed IDs, `_focusedInputId`, `_activeId`
   - `EditorDef<T>`: expression-tree-compiled getter/setter pairs for type-safe data binding
   - `SuppressMouseLeft` / `SuppressKeyboard`: gates in InputSystem for UI click/key suppression
   - SDL text input: switched from `EventType.Textinput` (unreliable on Linux/IME) to char-from-sym via `EventType.Keydown`
   - Player movement: force-based → direct velocity control (impulse + MoveTowards acceleration + exponential brake)
   - Physics: drag is `v *= exp(-drag * dt)`, `drag` is decay rate in s⁻¹
   - VoronoiTessellator: `BuildAsteroid(int sides, float radius, FractureProperties material, Func<Vector2,bool>? membership, Random rng)` — takes `sides` (random convex polygon vertex count) and `radius`, NOT the ProceduralAsteroidConfig shape params
   - Phase 4 = wiring `GameConfig` editor changes to live simulation (materials, weapons, player, asteroid spawn)

       ```csharp
       public bool IsHeld(KeyCode key)    => !SuppressKeyboard && _committed.Contains(key);
       public bool IsPressed(KeyCode key) =>
           (!SuppressKeyboard || IsEditingKey(key)) && _pressedThisFrame.Contains(key);
       public bool IsReleased(KeyCode key) =>
           (!SuppressKeyboard || IsEditingKey(key)) && _releasedThisFrame.Contains(key);
       ```

       ```csharp
       private static char SdlSymToChar(int sym) => sym switch {
           >= 97 and <= 122 => (char)sym,  // a-z
           >= 48 and <= 57  => (char)sym,  // 0-9
           95 => '_', 45 => '-', 32 => ' ', _ => '\0'
       };
       ```

     - `PlayerControlSystem.Update` — new arcade movement:
       ```csharp
       // Instant impulse on first press
       if (freshPress) vel.Linear += wantDir * _cfg.Impulse.Value;
       // Sustained acceleration (MoveTowards)
       float step = _cfg.Thrust.Value * fdt;
       Vector2 target = wantDir * _cfg.MaxSpeed.Value;
       Vector2 diff = target - vel.Linear;
       float diffLen = diff.Length();
       vel.Linear += diffLen <= step ? diff : diff / diffLen * step;
       // Hard speed cap
       float spd = vel.Linear.Length();
       if (spd > _cfg.MaxSpeed.Value) vel.Linear *= _cfg.MaxSpeed.Value / spd;
       // Exponential brake when no keys held
       vel.Linear *= MathF.Exp(-_cfg.Brake.Value * fdt);
       ```

     - NOTE: `BrakeDrag=0.85f` means "multiplier per second" in old system, but new system uses exponential decay rate (s⁻¹). Phase 4 will need `Impulse` field added and defaults updated.

4. Errors and fixes:
   - **Wrong Editor constructor signature**: Program.cs had `new Editor(gameConfig, assetsDir)` but new constructor requires `(GameConfig, Dictionary<string, ShapeData>, string)`. Fixed: captured shapes from Load and passed them.
   - **`ref` on C# properties not allowed**: `ref wave.Budget`, `ref wave.RapidInterval`, `ref wave.Boss`, `ref ast.DensityMult` — properties can't be passed as ref to Slider/Toggle. Fixed using local variable pattern: `float budget = wave.Budget; if (_ui.Slider(..., ref budget, ...)) { wave.Budget = budget; ... }`.
   - **Escape-cancel infinite loop**: Pressing Escape in rename mode defocused the TextInput widget (`_focusedInputId = 0`) but `_editingName` remained set, causing `autoFocus` to re-grab focus next frame. Fixed by checking `!_ui.IsTextInputActive` after TextInput call and clearing `_editingName` / `_renameIsNew`.
   - **Text input showing "strange characters"**: SDL `EventType.Textinput` reading via `Marshal.PtrToStringUTF8((IntPtr)(&ev.Text.Text))` was unreliable on Linux (confirmed struct layout was correct at offset 12, but may be affected by IME/IBus). Fixed by switching to KeyDown-derived chars via `SdlSymToChar` helper — bypasses SDL text input system entirely.
   - **WASD typing into text field**: When text input was active, WASD movement keys also fired SDL_TEXTINPUT events, typing into the rename field. Fixed by adding `SuppressKeyboard` to InputSystem (set from `editor.IsTextInputActive`) which blocks all non-editing keys.
   - **Player unresponsive**: With `LinDrag = 0.05` and `Mass = 12`, force-based thrust of 900 gave terminal velocity 1500 px/s but took 22+ seconds to approach. Fixed by redesigning PlayerControlSystem with direct velocity control (impulse + MoveTowards + exponential brake), setting `LinearDrag = 0` for player, and skipping player in TunableApplySystem.

5. Problem Solving:
   - **Click suppression architecture**: Geometry-based `IsMouseOverPanel()` approach — pure math check, no 1-frame lag, no draw-state dependency.
   - **Text input character derivation**: For ASCII-only game editor names, `SdlSymToChar` from KeyDown syms is sufficient and more reliable than the SDL text input pipeline on Linux. SDL syms 97-122 are always lowercase letters; key repeat fires additional KeyDown events automatically.
   - **Player movement arcade feel**: Direct velocity manipulation bypasses the physics drag accumulation. MoveTowards-based acceleration gives linear ramp rate (predictable). Exponential `exp(-brake * dt)` gives smooth deceleration. Tunable Impulse (130 px/s), Thrust (2200 px/s²), MaxSpeed (650 px/s), Brake (6.0 s⁻¹) give responsive arcade feel.
   - **Phase 4 design**: VoronoiTessellator.BuildAsteroid takes only `sides`, `radius`, and `FractureProperties` — ProceduralAsteroidConfig roughness/noiseFrequency etc. are not currently supported by the tessellator. Phase 4 wiring will use `materialKey` component on asteroids plus per-frame sync of `GameConfig.Materials` → `FracturableBody.Material`. Weapon params come from `GameConfig.Weapons[startingWeapon]`. Player params from `GameConfig.Player`.

   - *(Session resumed from context summary — implied continue from where left off)*

About the player movement: the feeling is wrong and it feels highly unresponsive (even if the tunable parameters aren't live yet). I think it needs some kind of instant impulse when pressing a key, the thrust should be just for acceleration. The inertia should also be highly limited."
   - "The impulse applied when pressing a key should be tunable as well. Now we can move on to phase 4."

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-11 16:41 UTC

Phase 4 is live. Here's what changed:

**Player movement** — `PlayerControlSystem` now reads `Impulse`, `Thrust`, `MaxSpeed`, `BrakeDrag` directly from `GameConfig.Player`. Adjusting those sliders in the Player editor tab takes effect immediately, no respawn needed.

**Weapon profile** — `OnBulletHit` and `PlayerControlSystem` now pull `Directionality`, `MomentumTransfer`, `EjectFraction`, `ImpactSpin`, `BlastFraction`, `FireRate`, `ProjectileSpeed`, and `TimeToLive` from `GameConfig.Weapons[startingWeapon]`. The Tuner panel's BulletMass/EnergyScale remain the energy intensity knob (unit calibration is a separate concern).

**Typed asteroid spawn** — `SpawnWave()` picks randomly from all procedural types in `GameConfig.Asteroids`. Each spawned body gets an `AsteroidTypeKey` component with its type name. Size comes from `SizeRange`, spin from `SpinRange`, material from the type's `material` key, outline polygon sides from `VertexCount`. Each material type gets a distinct color (rock=brown, ice=blue, metal=dark-grey, glass=green-tint).

**Live material sync** — every fixed step, after `TunableApplySystem` runs, a loop iterates all `FracturableBody + AsteroidTypeKey` entities and pushes the current `GameConfig.Materials[type.material]` values onto the live component. Bond strengths are recalculated immediately. Editing any material slider in the Materials tab now affects all running asteroids of that material in real time.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
- C# 2D physics/destruction engine: ECS (World, Entity, ISystem, EventBus), fixed timestep at 1/120s
- Cell/bond-graph Voronoi fracture model — `FracturableBody` with `Cell[]` and `Bond[]`
- `VoronoiTessellator.Build(IReadOnlyList<Vector2> convexBound, FractureProperties, membership, rng)` requires a convex outline
- `VoronoiTessellator.BuildAsteroid(int sides, float radius, ...)` generates random convex polygon internally
- `PolygonUtils.ClipConvexByHalfPlane` — Sutherland-Hodgman, requires convex input polygon
- `ShapeData`: authored shape with non-convex `Outline` (float[][]) + explicit `Seeds` (SeedData[]) with per-seed BondMult, BlastResist, DensityMult
- `GameConfig` (pure data library): JSON source of truth loaded via `GameConfigLoader.Load(assetsDir)` returning `(GameConfig, Dictionary<string, ShapeData>)`; shapes keyed by filename stem
- Immediate-mode UI: `Ui.cs` with FNV-1a hashed IDs; `EditorDef<T>` for type-safe binding
- Phase 4 architecture: `AsteroidTypeKey` component tags asteroids with type key; per-frame `SyncMaterial` loop overrides `TunableApplySystem` values for typed asteroids
- Player movement: direct velocity control — impulse on key press + MoveTowards acceleration + exponential brake (`exp(-BrakeDrag * dt)`)
- Gradual rotation: aim direction rotates toward mouse at `RotSpeed` rad/s (rate-limited)
- `WeaponProfile` fields (Directionality, MomentumTransfer, etc.) now read from `GameConfig.Weapons[startingWeapon]`; `bulletMass` still from `_cfg.BulletMass * _cfg.EnergyScale`
- Collision layers: `Asteroid = 1, Player = 2, Ghost = 4`
- `CompoundShape`: one `PolygonShape` per Voronoi cell, built by `VoronoiTessellator.BuildShape(FracturableBody)`

  ```csharp
          SyncMaterial(ref fb, mc);
      });
  }
  ```

  ```csharp
  Vector2 targetDir = Vector2.Normalize(toMouse);
  float targetAngle  = MathF.Atan2(targetDir.Y, targetDir.X);
  float currentAngle = MathF.Atan2(aim.Dir.Y, aim.Dir.X);
  float delta = targetAngle - currentAngle;
  while (delta >  MathF.PI) delta -= MathF.Tau;
  while (delta < -MathF.PI) delta += MathF.Tau;
  float maxTurn = p.RotSpeed * fdt;
  float turn = MathF.Abs(delta) <= maxTurn ? delta : MathF.Sign(delta) * maxTurn;
  aim.Dir = new Vector2(MathF.Cos(currentAngle + turn), MathF.Sin(currentAngle + turn));
  ```

4. Errors and fixes:
- **CS0841 "Cannot use local variable 'gameConfig' before it is declared"**: `DemoSession` was constructed using `gameConfig` before the `GameConfigLoader.Load` call. Fixed by moving the load block before `DemoSession` construction.
- **Nullable Remove crash in weapon/skill editors** (`InvalidOperationException: Nullable object must have a value`): The `has` variable was captured before the Remove button click. After clicking Remove (which nulls the nullable fields), `has` remained `true` and the slider block accessed `.Value` on a now-null nullable. Fixed by adding `has = false;` inside every removal branch for all 6 nullable sections.
- **Player Revert missing Impulse and StartingWeapon**: `OnRevert case 4` only copied Thrust/RotSpeed/MaxSpeed/BrakeDrag. Fixed by adding Impulse and StartingWeapon.
- **Wave Revert not reverting MaxLiveCells**: Fixed by adding `_config.MaxLiveCells = fresh.MaxLiveCells;` to case 6.

5. Problem Solving:
- **Phase 4 material sync architecture**: `TunableApplySystem` runs last in the system loop applying `_cfg` (Tuner) material values to ALL `FracturableBody` entities. The material sync for typed asteroids runs AFTER the system loop, overriding TunableApply's values with GameConfig material values for asteroids that have an `AsteroidTypeKey` component.
- **Weapon energy calibration deferred**: `WeaponConfig.Energy` (1200 for cannon) uses different units from `bulletMass` (0.20 in demo). Rather than break calibration, Phase 4 keeps `bulletMass = _cfg.BulletMass.Value * _cfg.EnergyScale.Value` and only wires the directional/profile fields + shot parameters (speed, firerate, TTL) from GameConfig.
- **Non-convex shape tessellation**: The `VoronoiTessellator.Build` method requires a convex bound because `ClipConvexByHalfPlane` is Sutherland-Hodgman which only works on convex inputs. For authored shapes (player ship, drone, bruiser) with non-convex outlines, the solution requires: (1) compute convex hull of outline as tessellation boundary, (2) use explicit seeds from ShapeData instead of ScatterSeeds, (3) apply per-seed BondMult to bonds and per-seed BlastResist/DensityMult to cells. This requires: adding `ConvexHull` to `PolygonUtils`, adding `BuildFromShape` to `VoronoiTessellator`, and possibly adding BlastResist/DensityMult fields to `Cell`.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-12 12:27 UTC

Here's what was done:

**`PolygonUtils.cs`** — Added `ConvexHull(IReadOnlyList<Vector2>)` using Andrew's monotone chain (O(n log n)). Returns CW-wound hull matching engine convention.

**`VoronoiTessellator.cs`** — Added `BuildFromExplicitSeeds(outline, seedPositions, seedBondMults, material, rng)`:
- Computes convex hull of the outline (handles non-convex authored shapes)
- Uses the explicit seed positions as Voronoi sites instead of random scatter
- Builds bonds with per-seed strength scaling: `EdgeLength × toughness × √(mult_i × mult_j)`. The cockpit's BondMult=5 makes bonds around it ~2.2× nominal strength; bumpers at BondMult=2 are ~1.4× stronger; propellers at ~1.9× are moderately reinforced.

**`Program.cs`**:
- `DemoSession` now accepts `shapes` dict and passes it to `SpawnPlayer`
- `SpawnPlayer` tessellates `player_ship.json` via `BuildFromExplicitSeeds` — the ship gets a `FracturableBody + CompoundShape` collider in blue, with proper mass/inertia from the metal material
- Falls back to circle collider if the shape file is missing
- `TunableApplySystem` skips `PlayerTag` entities in the `FracturableBody` loop (prevents Tuner from overwriting the player's metal material with rock defaults)
- `OnFractureCompleted`/`OnFractureSplit` guard against the player entity
- Renderer skips the circle draw when the player has a `FracturableBody` (the cell mesh is drawn by the asteroid render pass)
- Renamed `playership.json` → `player_ship.json` to match the config key

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-12 13:00 UTC

Two distinct problems:

**Shape looks square**: The convex hull of the playership outline is nearly a rectangle (extreme points at ±80 X, ±75 Y). Voronoi cells clipped to a rectangle = rectangular blobs. The ship's non-convex silhouette is completely invisible.

**No rotation**: `Transform.Rotation` is driven by `Velocity.Angular` (physics), which has nothing to do with `AimComponent.Dir`. The aim indicator rotates but the cell mesh doesn't.

The rotation fix is trivial — zero `vel.Angular` and set `t.Rotation = aimAngle` in `PlayerControlSystem`.

The shape problem is architectural. The Voronoi approach fundamentally can't represent non-convex shapes well. The user's suggestion is right: **switch to explicit cell polygons in the shape file**. Instead of `outline + seeds`, the shape editor authors each cell directly as a convex polygon:

```json
{
  "name": "PlayerShip",
  "cells": [
    { "vertices": [[x,y], ...], "role": "cockpit", "bondMult": 5 },
    { "vertices": [[x,y], ...], "role": "cannon",  "bondMult": 2 },
    ...
  ]
}
```

Bonds are found at load time by detecting shared edges. No Voronoi needed. The ship looks exactly as authored.

The shape editor (browser prototype) would need to output this format instead of seeds. Let me check what's there:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-12 13:01 UTC

The editor already computes Voronoi cells internally via `buildVoronoi()` — it just doesn't export them. The fix is to export the computed cell polygons directly, so the C# engine uses them as-is instead of re-tessellating.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-12 13:02 UTC

Found the root cause. The JS editor clips `voronoiCell` against the **original non-convex outline** directly. My C# `BuildFromExplicitSeeds` computes the convex hull first — that's why the shape becomes a rectangle. The hull of the ship is essentially `(±80, ±75)`.

Fix is simple: drop the hull computation and pass `outline` directly to `VoronoiCell`, exactly matching what the JS does. Plus fix the rotation sync.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-12 13:03 UTC

Clean. Summary of what was wrong and what's fixed:

**Shape was a rectangle**: `BuildFromExplicitSeeds` computed the convex hull of the outline and used that as the Voronoi boundary. The hull of the ship is nearly `(±80, ±75)` — a rectangle. Fixed by passing the outline directly to `VoronoiCell`, exactly matching the JS shape editor's `voronoiCell(s, allSeeds, outline)`. Now cells are clipped to the actual ship silhouette.

**Ship didn't rotate with aim**: The `FracturableBody` cell mesh rotates with `Transform.Rotation`, but that was driven by physics (`vel.Angular`), not the aim direction. Fixed by: zeroing `vel.Angular` every frame, and writing `t.Rotation = Atan2(aim.Dir)` after the aim update. `Inertia = 0` prevents asteroid collisions from imparting spin.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-12 13:38 UTC

Done. Three changes:

1. **Direction**: `t.Rotation = Atan2(aim.Y, aim.X) + π/2` — the `+π/2` offset compensates for the ship being authored nose-up (−Y) so it aligns with the engine's right-facing default aim. When the cursor is above the ship, the nose points up; to the right, the nose points right — as expected.

2. **Scale**: `PlayerConfig.ShapeScale = 0.5` (default) is multiplied into both the outline and seed coordinates before tessellating. At 0.5× the ship goes from ±80px to ±40px. There's a **Shape Scale** slider in the Player editor tab (0.1–2×) so you can tune it live without restarting — note that scale changes take effect on next respawn since it's baked into the geometry at spawn time.

3. The `game_config.json` default is already 0.5 via the `PlayerConfig` model default. If you want to persist a different value, adjust it in the editor and save.

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-12 14:01 UTC

Let's go back to the game design: I put some thought into how I want the game to work and these are some new directions. Give me honest feedback, suggestions, complications if there's any and doability analysis.

## New notes that may change other parts

A typical run lasts around 12 minutes, at 10 minutes, independently on how many waves the player cleared, the mothership spawns. Special waves (explicit waves) spawn at fixed points during the game. After the boss fight endless mode starts, with fast scaling of waves.

### World

The world is 5760x3240. All asteroids "orbit" around the center and are pulled laterally and back into the center exponentially more the greater their distance from the world center. This would give movement to asteroids and make them concentrate in the center of the map.
This would be just a system that applies forces to all bodies in the game based on their distance from the center of the map.
The border of the map has a flat bounce as fallback for when objects reach it, shouldn't happen normally though.

### Waves

Max live cells: as the game progresses, the cap on the number of live cells raises, so the later waves are far more chaotic than the beginning. Start with 300 max live cells, increment at the end of each wave by around 30. No more than 2000.

Wave budget: asteroid types have a cost, multiplied by their "size_multiplier". Incremented at the end of each wave.

WaveSystem: has internal timer. every 5 seconds or so, check the number of current live cells -> if <= 30% current_max_cells: spawn_new wave and reset timer. 
if 30 seconds passed from last wave spawn: spawn new wave and reset timer.

After every spawn raise wave_budget and max_live_cells

SpawnWave: the most difficult and flexible part. 
1. Choosing the asteroids: based on how much time has passed since the beginning of the run, the pool of available asteroids/aliens is increased.
2. Each asteroid/alien type has a cost, paid with the wave budget. For asteroids there is a "size_multiplier" (or something like that) that multiplies its area and number of vertices and cells. It increases its cost accordingly.
3. Bias when choosing: the wave manager must maximize the wave cost, the count of new asteroids and new cells. Constraints: wave_budget, current_max_cells, wave_count_max. Need to also guarantee variety in some way. 
4. Spawn position: For each asteroid select a position: close to the border (so the orbit system gives him movement), strictly outside of the camera view, no other body collides with it.
5. Special waves: explicit waves are based purely based on how much time has passed from the beginning of the run:
Something like: around 3 minutes in the first horde wave spawns, 5 minutes in a large group of heavily spinning small asteroids, at 7 minutes a big group of alien ships spawn all together, at 10 minutes the mothership spawns.

### Upgrade system

We can stub this one for now.
At the end of each wave (beginning of a new one) the game pauses and the user can choose an upgrade chosen at random from a pool (faster fire rate, more energy, new weapons, ammo for some weapon etc.). This will give a feeling of progression to the player and enables various "builds".

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-12 14:02 UTC

Good foundation. Here's honest section-by-section analysis:

---

## Run structure (12 min, fixed-timestamp events)

**Strong.** Fixed-time boss regardless of wave count is a proven pattern — it creates definitive pressure and prevents turtling. Works well with the wave system you described.

**Gap:** What happens on player death? The whole run structure assumes the player survives to 10 min. Does death end the run? Restart from wave 1? This needs a decision before the wave system makes sense to implement.

**Doability:** Trivial — a global timer + state enum.

---

## World (5760×3240, orbital gravity, border bounce)

**The orbital gravity idea is the most interesting thing here and also the trickiest to tune.**

"Pulled laterally and back to center exponentially more the greater their distance" — I'd call this a vortex force field: centripetal component (pulls toward center) + tangential component (rotates around center). Combined, objects spiral inward rather than fall straight in. That's a good feel.

**Problems:**
- **Exponential is wrong.** Exponential growth at 2880px from center (half the world width) would produce astronomically large forces. Use linear or quadratic with a distance cap. Something like `F = k * clamp(dist - deadzone, 0, max_dist)` is predictable and tunable.
- **The tangential/centripetal ratio is everything.** Too much tangential → stable orbit loops that never converge. Too much centripetal → everything piles at the center in seconds. The equilibrium between them needs careful testing.
- **Fragments inherit this too.** When an asteroid shatters, 20 fragments all get the vortex force. At high cell counts this is fine; just noting it's not a separate concern.

**Big gap that affects everything: no camera system in the design.**  
5760×3240 with a 1920×1080 window means the player sees 1/9th of the world. Where does the camera point? Player-centered? Fixed? Free-roaming? This is a prerequisite for the spawn system ("spawn outside camera view") and for the UI/minimap question. It's not a difficult decision but it needs to be made explicitly.

**Border bounce:** Fine as a safety net. Simple to implement.

**Doability:** World size + vortex force — easy to implement, hard to tune well. Camera — needs a design decision first.

---

## Wave system

**The core logic is solid.** Poll every 5 seconds / force spawn after 30 seconds / scale budget and cell cap after each wave — this is clean and produces good pacing. One small note: polling every 5 seconds introduces up to 5 seconds of artificial dead time after the field clears. You could simplify to: "when live cells drop below threshold, start a 5-second countdown, then spawn" — same feel, no polling loop.

**Max live cells:** 300 start, +30 per wave, cap 2000. At roughly one wave every 30 seconds for 10 minutes, you'd hit around wave 20 before the mothership, giving ~900 max cells. That's reasonable. The cap of 2000 means late-game endless mode gets intense but not infinite.

**Budget + cost system:** You haven't specified starting budget or increment amount. This is the most important number to get right — it determines whether the game feels too easy or impossible. You'll need to iterate on these empirically. The "size multiplier multiplies cost" idea is clean; it naturally means a big boulder costs more than small gravel.

**"Maximize cost + count + cells while guaranteeing variety"** is a bin-packing variant, which is NP-hard to solve optimally. In practice: greedy works fine. Sort available types by cost-efficiency, fill greedily, then enforce variety with a soft rule like "each type available in the pool has at least a 15% probability weight." Don't over-engineer this.

**Spawn position (outside camera view):** This is blocked on the camera design. Can't implement "outside camera frustum" without knowing where the camera is.

**Time-gated content pool:** Very easy. A lookup table of `(time_seconds → unlock type_key)`.

**Doability:** Wave timer and scaling — easy. Budget fill algorithm — medium. Spawn positioning — needs camera first.

---

## Upgrade system (stub)

**The idea is right and the stub call is the right call now.**  
One practical complication to flag for later: pausing a physics simulation mid-wave and resuming cleanly requires the fixed-timestep loop to be interruptible. Currently the game loop doesn't have a pause concept. Not hard to add — just needs a `_paused` flag checked before stepping — but worth noting.

---

## What's not in the design but will be needed

1. **Camera:** player-follow with dead zone? zoom level? This affects spawn positions, minimap, and the vortex visual feel.
2. **Player death / lives:** the whole run structure depends on this.
3. **Budget starting values and increment amounts:** you'll need concrete numbers, even rough ones, to start tuning.
4. **Alien wave behavior:** waves 6–7 reference drones/bruisers. Their AI (steering, targeting) hasn't been designed yet — this is a significant implementation chunk.

---

## Overall verdict

The design is coherent and implementable. The vortex world is distinctive and worth building. The main thing I'd push back on: **get the camera and player-death decisions made before touching the wave system** — both designs reference those as implicit facts and they'll shape the implementation significantly. Everything else can be built incrementally.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-12 14:56 UTC

The decisions are clean. Here's targeted feedback on the estimates and a few technical clarifications:

---

## Budget math has a discrepancy

Wave 10 target is 75, but your own example computes to more:
```
(10×1 + 7×3 + 4×4 + 3×5) × 1.5avg_size = 62 × 1.5 = 93
```
For 75, the average size multiplier would need to be ~1.21, not 1.5. Either:
- The starting budget should be higher (30 instead of 25), or
- The size average at wave 10 should be closer to 1.2 (which is actually plausible since SizeRange for most types goes 0.6–1.4), or
- You accept that 93 is fine and the estimates were rough

The last option is probably right — these are tuning targets, not contracts. The framework is correct.

---

## Size multiplier definition needs pinning

"Double the default area = double the cost" — but the engine currently uses `SizeRange` as a **radius** multiplier: `radius = BaseRadius × size`. Area scales as radius², so:

- If `size_mult = 1.5` is a **radius** multiplier: actual area = 1.5² = 2.25× base. Cost = base × 2.25.
- If `size_mult = 1.5` is an **area** multiplier: radius = √1.5 ≈ 1.22× base.

These give very different costs. You need to decide which `size_mult` means. I'd recommend keeping it as a **radius multiplier** (it's more intuitive to "make the asteroid 1.5× bigger"), and computing cost as `base_cost × size²` so that area-doubling doubles cost.

---

## Cell count scaling is already solved

You noted "cell count should scale with size to maintain the same grain size." This already works — `ScatterSeeds` in the tessellator uses `GrainArea` to determine density. A 2× radius asteroid automatically gets ~4× the cells at the same grain size. The `SeedCount` field in `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` is actually not used at spawn time (the call goes through `ScatterSeeds` directly). You don't need to change anything here.

---

## Max live cells vs budget — they work at different scales

At wave 10 with ~25 asteroids, 7–8 cells each average, that's ~180 cells. Cell cap at wave 10 = 300 + 9×30 = 570 — plenty of headroom. The cell cap won't bite until ~wave 25–30. Good natural separation between budget (what you *want* to spawn) and cell cap (hard physics limit). No issues here.

---

## Natural implementation order

Before touching the wave system, two things are prerequisites:

**Phase 1 — World:**
- World resize 5760×3240 (trivial constant change)
- Camera follow with lag (transforms every render coordinate, prerequisite for spawn positioning)
- Vortex force field as a new `ISystem` (quadratic, capped)
- Spawn positions near the border and outside the camera frustum

**Phase 2 — Wave system:**
- Game timer + time-gated type pool
- Budget-based wave fill (greedy + variety weight)
- Size-adjusted cost at spawn time
- Cell cap increment + budget increment per wave

**Phase 3 — Timestamps/special waves** can be wired in after Phase 2.

The camera is the load-bearing prerequisite — without it, "spawn outside viewport" is undefined. Want to start there?
