This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:

This session continued "Asteroids on Steroids" — a C# 2D physics/destruction engine game. Work covered several phases:

**Phase 1 (shapes):** Implement compound fracturable player ship using `player_ship.json` authored shape: `BuildFromExplicitSeeds` on `VoronoiTessellator`, `ConvexHull` on `PolygonUtils`, `ShapeScale` on `PlayerConfig`, player rotation synced to aim.

**Phase 2 (ship fixes):** Fix ship rendering as a square (wrong Voronoi boundary), fix ship not rotating with aim, fix wrong facing direction (+π/2 offset), fix oversized ship (0.5× scale).

**Phase 3 (game design):** Feedback session on new game directions (5760×3240 world, vortex force, wave budget system, run structure). User confirmed: player death ends run; vortex = quadratic+cap; camera = player-follow with lag; wave polling fine; aliens deferred.

**Phase 4 (Phase 1 implementation, in progress):** World resize to 5760×3240, camera follow system, vortex force field, border bounce, border-zone asteroid spawning, camera offset applied to renderer.

---

2. Key Technical Concepts:
- C# ECS: `World`, `Entity`, `ISystem`, `EventBus`, fixed timestep at 1/120s
- Voronoi tessellation: `VoronoiCell` clips starting polygon by perpendicular bisectors of all seeds. Sutherland-Hodgman half-plane clipping.
- `FracturableBody`: `Cell[]` (Local verts, Centroid, Area) + `Bond[]` (A, B, EdgeLength, Strength) + `FractureProperties`
- `BuildFromExplicitSeeds`: uses the original non-convex outline directly as Voronoi boundary (matches JS shape editor's `voronoiCell` behavior)
- `BuildBondsWeighted`: bond strength = `EdgeLength × toughness × √(mult_i × mult_j)` (geometric mean of per-seed BondMult)
- Camera: world-space `Position` (screen center), `Offset = new(screenW/2 - pos.X, screenH/2 - pos.Y)`, exponential lag follow
- VortexSystem: centripetal + CCW tangential force proportional to `excess²` beyond deadzone. Applies to all `Transform + Velocity + RigidBody` entities.
- Camera offset pattern: `screenPos = worldPos + camera.Offset`
- Andrew's monotone chain for `ConvexHull` (O(n log n)), CW winding output
- `ShapeData`: `float[][] Outline`, `SeedData[]` with `X, Y, Role, BondMult, BlastResist, DensityMult`

---

3. Files and Code Sections:

- **`GameEngine/Engine/Collision/PolygonUtils.cs`**
  - Added `ConvexHull(IReadOnlyList<Vector2>)` (Andrew's monotone chain, CW output) and private `Cross2D` helper.
  - Also added in section between "Surface projection" and end of class.

- **`GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/VoronoiTessellator.cs`**
  - Added `BuildFromExplicitSeeds(outline, seedPositions, seedBondMults, material, rng)`:
    - Uses `outline` directly (NOT convex hull) as Voronoi boundary — matches JS editor
    - Fallback if all cells empty: `kept.Add(outline.ToArray()); keptIdx.Add(0);`
  - Added `BuildBondsWeighted(cells, seedIndices, mults, toughness)`:
    - `float bm = MathF.Sqrt(mi * mj); Strength = shared * toughness * bm;`

- **`GameEngine/Engine/Effects/ParticleSystem.cs`**
  - `Draw(IRenderer r)` → `Draw(IRenderer r, Vector2 offset = default)`
  - Each particle draws at `p.Position + offset`

  **GameConst** (updated):
  ```csharp
  static class GameConst
  {
      public const float PlayerRadius = 15f;
      public const int   WorldW = 5760, WorldH = 3240;
      public const int   ScreenW = 1920, ScreenH = 1080;
  }
  ```

  **Camera class** (new):
  ```csharp
  sealed class Camera
  {
      public Vector2 Position;   // world-space coordinate of the screen centre
      public float   FollowSpeed = 4f;
      private readonly float _hw, _hh;
      private readonly float _minX, _minY, _maxX, _maxY;
      public Camera(Vector2 startPos, int screenW, int screenH) { ... clamped init ... }
      public void Update(Vector2 target, float dt)
      {
          target = Vector2.Clamp(target, new Vector2(_minX, _minY), new Vector2(_maxX, _maxY));
          Position += (target - Position) * (1f - MathF.Exp(-FollowSpeed * dt));
      }
      public Vector2 Offset => new(_hw - Position.X, _hh - Position.Y);
      public bool IsVisible(Vector2 worldPos, float radius = 0f) { ... }
  }
  ```

  **VortexSystem class** (new):
  ```csharp
  sealed class VortexSystem : ISystem
  {
      private readonly Vector2 _centre;
      private readonly float _deadzone;      // inner radius — no force inside (default 900f)
      private readonly float _centripetalK;  // accel = k × excess² (default 2.5e-5f)
      private readonly float _tangentialK;   // accel = k × excess² (default 1.5e-5f)
      public VortexSystem(Vector2 centre, float deadzone=900f, float centripetalK=2.5e-5f, float tangentialK=1.5e-5f) { ... }
      public void Update(World world, double dt)
      {
          world.ForEach<Transform, Velocity, RigidBody>((Entity _, ref Transform t, ref Velocity v, ref RigidBody _) =>
          {
              Vector2 toCenter = _centre - t.Position;
              float dist = toCenter.Length(); if (dist < 1e-3f) return;
              float excess = dist - _deadzone; if (excess <= 0f) return;
              Vector2 radial  = toCenter / dist;
              Vector2 tangent = new(-radial.Y, radial.X);  // CCW
              float mag = excess * excess;
              v.Linear += (_centripetalK * radial + _tangentialK * tangent) * mag * fdt;
          });
      }
  }
  ```

  **BorderBounceSystem class** (new):
  ```csharp
  sealed class BorderBounceSystem : ISystem
  {
      public void Update(World world, double dt)
      {
          world.ForEach<Transform, Velocity>((Entity _, ref Transform t, ref Velocity v) =>
          {
              if (t.Position.X < 0f)               { t.Position.X = 0f;                v.Linear.X =  MathF.Abs(v.Linear.X); }
              if (t.Position.X > GameConst.WorldW)  { t.Position.X = GameConst.WorldW; v.Linear.X = -MathF.Abs(v.Linear.X); }
              if (t.Position.Y < 0f)               { t.Position.Y = 0f;                v.Linear.Y =  MathF.Abs(v.Linear.Y); }
              if (t.Position.Y > GameConst.WorldH)  { t.Position.Y = GameConst.WorldH; v.Linear.Y = -MathF.Abs(v.Linear.Y); }
          });
      }
  }
  ```

  **DemoSession** (updated fields/constructor):
  ```csharp
  private readonly int _screenW, _screenH;  // was _w, _h
  private Camera _camera;
  private static readonly Vector2 WorldCenter = new(GameConst.WorldW * 0.5f, GameConst.WorldH * 0.5f);
  public Camera Camera => _camera;
  
  public DemoSession(int screenW, int screenH, InputSystem input, Config cfg, GameConfig gc, Dictionary<string, ShapeData> shapes)
  {
      _screenW = screenW; _screenH = screenH; _cfg = cfg; _gc = gc; _shapes = shapes;
      _camera = new Camera(WorldCenter, screenW, screenH);
      SpawnPlayer(WorldCenter);
      SpawnWave();
      _systems = new ISystem[] {
          new PreviousStateSystem(),
          new PlayerControlSystem(input, _player, cfg, gc),
          new PhysicsSystem(),
          new VortexSystem(WorldCenter),       // NEW
          new MovementSystem(),
          new BorderBounceSystem(),            // NEW
          new RaycastBulletSystem(...),
          new GhostSystem(),
          new CollisionSystem(...),
          ...
      };
  }
  ```

  **DemoSession.Update** — camera update added:

---

4. Errors and fixes:
- **CS0841 `hull` used before declared**: After removing the ConvexHull call in `BuildFromExplicitSeeds`, the fallback `kept.Add(hull)` still referenced the now-removed `hull` variable. Fixed: `kept.Add(outline.ToArray())`.
- **Shape renders as square**: Root cause: `BuildFromExplicitSeeds` computed `ConvexHull(outline)` (nearly rectangular for the ship), then Voronoi-tessellated within that hull → rectangular cells. The JS shape editor clips to the original non-convex outline directly. Fix: remove hull computation, pass `outline` directly to `VoronoiCell`.
- **Ship not rotating with aim**: `Transform.Rotation` was driven by physics angular velocity, not aim direction. Fix: `vel.Angular = 0f` + `t.Rotation = Atan2(aim.Dir.Y, aim.Dir.X) + π/2`.
- **Wrong facing direction**: Ship designed facing up (−Y). +π/2 rotation offset aligns up→right for default aim direction (UnitX). Derived mathematically: local (0,−R) → screen (+R, 0) when `rot = π/2`.
- **Shape too large**: Ship vertices at ±80px. Fixed with `ShapeScale = 0.5f` in PlayerConfig, applied as scale multiplier at spawn.
- **`playership.json` vs `player_ship`**: GameConfig had `"shape": "player_ship"` but file was named `playership.json`. Fixed by renaming file to `player_ship.json`.

---

5. Problem Solving:
- **Project dependency constraint**: Engine can't reference GameConfig (circular). Solved by `BuildFromExplicitSeeds` taking primitive `Vector2` arrays — game layer does ShapeData → Vector2 conversion.
- **TunableApplySystem overwriting player material**: Player material is metal (toughness=40), but TunableApplySystem iterated all FracturableBody entities and overwrote with tuner rock values. Fixed by `if (world.HasComponent<PlayerTag>(e)) return;` in the FracturableBody loop.
- **SyncMaterial + per-seed BondMult**: SyncMaterial recalculates bonds as `EdgeLength × toughness` — would flatten per-seed BondMult scaling. Solution: player has PlayerTag so it's not touched by typed-asteroid sync loop; TunableApplySystem skips it. Player bonds stay at spawn-time values (already encode metal toughness + BondMult).
- **Camera as prerequisite**: "Spawn outside viewport" requires camera. Now implemented. World size and camera are both done, enabling proper spawn positioning.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-12 16:22 UTC

Clean. Here's what changed and why it's better:

**Formula**: was `k × excess²`, now `k × excess`. Quadratic gives nearly zero force close to the deadzone edge and only kicks in far out — you'd barely notice it at 100–200px past the boundary. Linear gives immediate, proportional force the moment an asteroid crosses. At excess = 500px with the default `centripetalK = 0.10`, that's 50 px/s² inward — enough to visibly bend trajectories.

**Three new tuner params under `-- VORTEX --`**:
- `Deadzone` (100–2800, step 50) — the radius inside which no force is applied
- `Centripetal k` (0–0.50, step 0.01) — inward pull strength
- `Tangential k` (0–0.30, step 0.01) — CCW swirl strength

All three read live every frame, so you can dial them in-game with arrow keys without restarting.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-13 11:39 UTC

Confirmed: the Tuner's player section is vestigial — actual player reads from `GameConfig.Player`. Now I have a clear picture.

**My proposal before implementing:**

**Border:** Replace the hard bounce with per-axis velocity damping — when an entity is within 200px of a wall, only the outward component of velocity is bled exponentially (factor `0 → 1` as distance `zone → 0`). No counter-force, so no bouncing. At the actual wall face the damping rate per second is `e^(-k)` — very fast asteroid (600 px/s) will be slowed to nearly nothing well before the wall. Hard position clamp is just a safety net.

**Player:** Ship-relative axes + passive lateral drag applied every frame. The elegant insight: lateral velocity bleeds continuously at rate `LateralDrag` (s⁻¹) regardless of input. Pressing A/D fights against this drain and reaches a speed ceiling of `Thrust × LateralFactor / LateralDrag` — much lower than forward max. The moment you stop pressing A/D the lateral momentum drains quickly. Forward momentum persists. Numbers: Thrust 4500, MaxSpeed 900, Impulse 250, LateralDrag 5, LateralFactor 0.30. At steady state that gives ~270 px/s lateral vs 900 forward — noticeably sluggish but still steerable.

Sound good?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-13 11:41 UTC

What movement aspect would you like to adjust? The lateral ceiling speed (currently ~270 px/s via LateralFactor/LateralDrag), how quickly lateral bleeds when you release A/D, the reverse behavior, or something else?

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-13 13:48 UTC

The main question with the movement is: should "W" move the ship in the direction it's facing or always up. Would it make sense to make it always move up but consider it as lateral or backwards based on the direction it's facing?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-13 13:49 UTC

This is the key design question. There are really two distinct philosophies:

**Option A — W = world up, always**
WASD moves in fixed world directions. But whether that movement costs "full thrust" or reduced thrust depends on how it aligns with your facing direction. Facing up and pressing W = forward efficiency. Facing right and pressing W = that's lateral relative to your aim, so it gets the lateral drag treatment. The incentive to face your direction of travel comes from the passive drag on velocity that's perpendicular to aim — not from which key you pressed.

**Option B — W = ship forward, always**
Classic twin-stick. The keys rotate with the ship. Snappy and direct but WASD changes meaning as you spin, which can disorient.

**My recommendation: Option A.** It's more interesting and better suited to this game. The ship aims with the mouse for shooting, independently of movement. If W always means "up", the player never loses track of their controls. The directional efficiency penalty comes for free from the passive lateral drag — it's just that "lateral" is defined relative to aim, not relative to the pressed key. You press W, ship goes up, but if you're facing sideways that velocity is perpendicular to aim and bleeds off faster. The natural consequence: players learn to face the direction they're moving to preserve momentum — without the controls ever feeling inverted.

**Concrete feel:** sprinting upward while aiming right (at an asteroid) works fine, but the moment you stop pressing W that lateral-to-aim momentum drains. Facing up while pressing W keeps you efficient indefinitely.

Want me to implement that — world-space WASD with passive drag applied to the aim-perpendicular component of velocity?

Implement the border, leaving the vortex force as-is, and Option A, your recommendation.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-13 13:55 UTC

Clean. Summary of what's in:

**Border (`BorderDampSystem`):** Replaces the hard bounce. Each wall has a 200px zone. When an entity moves toward a wall inside that zone, only the outward velocity component is multiplied by `exp(-20 × factor × dt)` where `factor` goes 0→1 as you approach the wall face. No force is added — momentum just drains. A 600 px/s asteroid entering the zone is reduced to near-zero before it can reach the wall.

**Movement (Option A):** WASD still maps to world up/down/left/right. But every frame, before thrust is applied, velocity is decomposed into aim-aligned and aim-perpendicular components, and the perpendicular part decays at `LateralDrag` s⁻¹. So if you're facing up and pressing W, all your velocity is aim-aligned — no drain, full efficiency. If you're facing right while pressing W (world-up), that velocity is perpendicular to aim and bleeds continuously. Turning to face your direction of travel removes the drain instantly.

New defaults: Thrust 4500 (was 2200), MaxSpeed 900 (was 650), Impulse 250 (was 130), BrakeDrag 4 (was 6), LateralDrag 6 (new). All tunable in the Player editor panel.

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-13 14:09 UTC

Now I understand: no matter how you tune the vortex forces, asteroids always accumulate a lot of speed and end up orbiting around the map. The vortex force shouldn't apply the force to objects that already have enough velocity in those directions. Needs a cap, maybe something like "if the object has the velocity that would result in staying inside the vortex at this distance for 100 frames, skip applying the forces". Of course it counts only if the velocity is in the same direction the vortex would apply its force to. What do you think?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-13 14:11 UTC

This is a sharp observation. The core issue: the tangential force never has anything opposing it — centripetal opposes outward drift but nothing opposes orbital spin-up, so objects accumulate CCW velocity indefinitely.

Your "100 frames" framing is exactly right and maps cleanly to code. The cap for each component is simply `100 × force_per_frame = k × excess × 100 × dt`. That's the velocity that 100 frames of continuous force at the current excess would produce. If the object's velocity projection onto the force direction already exceeds that, the vortex is done its job — skip.

The soft version (clamp the addition rather than skip entirely) avoids a discontinuity: when approaching the cap, only add what's left to reach it. One extra detail: the cap only applies when velocity is *already in the force direction* — if an object is moving outward (against centripetal), we always pull; if moving CW (against tangential), we always push CCW. Your parenthetical already specified this, and it falls out naturally from the projection.

I'll make `capFrames` tunable since you said "something like 100":

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-13 14:11 UTC

Now rewrite `VortexSystem.Update` with the capped application:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-13 14:12 UTC

Clean. Here's exactly what the cap does in numbers with default settings (centripetalK=0.10, excess=500, dt=1/120):

- `forceC = 0.10 × 500 × 1/120 ≈ 0.42 px/s` per frame  
- `capC = 0.42 × 100 = 41.7 px/s` inward

An asteroid already moving inward at 41.7 px/s toward the center gets no more centripetal pull — it's already returning fast enough. One moving outward (negative projection) always gets the full force. Same logic for tangential: once CCW orbital speed reaches `~25 px/s` at that excess, the spin-up stops. Objects further out get a proportionally higher cap, so the force is still strong enough to correct large excesses.

Tune `Cap frames` up for a lazier vortex that allows faster orbits, down for a tighter one that nearly freezes velocity at the cap.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-13 17:00 UTC

The simulation looks solid. Here are the key observations:

**What's working well:**
- Budget efficiency 95–100% for waves 6–20 — the algorithm almost never wastes budget
- Theme waves land correctly: wave 3 spawns 3–4 Boulders (large, slow), wave 5 fills the count cap with 10–11 Gravels, wave 7 is Armored-heavy, wave 9 is Spinner+Unstable chaos
- Size multipliers give natural intra-wave variety — you see `Gravel×2.9` (a big rattly pebble) alongside `Gravel` (tiny) which is interesting

**Two issues worth discussing:**

1. **Wave 5 only spends 65–71% of budget** (32/45). The count cap (13 slots) fills up with cheap Gravels before the budget runs out. This is actually fine for a horde wave — the point is quantity, not budget efficiency. But if it bothers you, dropping Gravel's base cost to 0.5 would let the budget push even more of them in.

2. **Wave 10 gives 8–10 asteroids, but the design doc targets 20–25.** The culprit is the countCap formula (`8 + wave = 18`) combined with the per-type variety cap eating the remaining slots. If you want 20–25 at wave 10, the countCap should be closer to `8 + wave * 2` (giving 28 at wave 10 — enough headroom). Or leave it and re-calibrate the doc expectation downward — 10 asteroids at wave 10 with some at ×1.5 size is actually denser in total area than 25 size-1 gravels.

**One structural question** before implementing: the `bias` vector in the function signature is passed in externally (the wave director owns it). Do you want `ChooseAsteroids` to be purely a budget-packing function that just receives a bias, or should the variety cap logic live inside it? Right now it's inside (the 45%-per-type rule), which means the caller can't override it for something like a strict mono-wave. If you'll want pure mono-waves (e.g., wave 7 = only Armored, no exceptions), the cap should be an input parameter or handled by the caller setting all other biases to zero.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-13 18:06 UTC

All good design calls. Let me think through the open questions and update the sim:

**Count → size_bias**: removing `countCap` means the cell cap alone controls how much the wave can spawn. `sizeBias` in [-1, +1] skews the size_mult sampling — implemented as a power distribution: `mult = 1 + rand^(2^(-sizeBias)) × (maxMult-1)`. At `sizeBias=0` that's uniform; `+1` biases toward large (few beefy asteroids); `-1` toward small (many cheap ones). This replaces the variety cap too.

**Rotation/velocity**: they live in the asteroid type's game_config entry, read by the spawn function. `ChooseAsteroids` is purely a packing function — returns `(type, size_mult)` pairs and nothing else. The spawn function owns world placement, velocity sampling, and spin.

**Wave loop formalized:**

```
WaveManager state:
  current_wave, last_spawn_time, live_cell_count, max_live_cells, wave_budget

poll every frame:
  if (live_cell_count <= 0.3 × max_live_cells) || (now - last_spawn_time > 30s):
      desc          = fetch_next_wave(current_wave, elapsed_run_time)
      remaining     = max_live_cells - live_cell_count   ← caller subtracts live
      asteroid_list = choose_asteroids(desc.budget, cost_table, desc.bias, desc.size_bias, remaining)
      spawn_wave(asteroid_list, camera)
      last_spawn_time = now
      max_live_cells += 30
      wave_budget    += 5
      current_wave   += 1
```

`fetch_next_wave` checks the timestamp table first (special waves at 3 min, 5 min, 7 min, 10 min), otherwise returns a budget wave with the bias for that wave number.

Now updating the sim — removing `countCap`, adding `sizeBias`:

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:

This session continued "Asteroids on Steroids" — a C# 2D physics/destruction arcade game. Work covered:

**Phase: Camera offset in DemoRenderer** (carried over from prior context): Apply world-to-screen camera offset to all rendered entities, add frustum culling. Then add background grid for motion feel.

**Phase: Player controls**: Fix aim direction not being relative to ship's screen position. Discuss and implement directional movement. Ultimately: revert to world-axis WASD with passive aim-relative lateral drag (Option A).

**Phase: Vortex force**: Make vortex deadzone and force constants tunable via the panel. Improve formula (quadratic → linear). Add per-component velocity cap so objects don't accumulate infinite orbital speed ("100 frames" cap).

**Phase: Border system**: Replace hard bounce with exponential velocity damping near walls — no counter-force, entities slow and stop rather than bounce.

**Phase: Wave simulation**: Plan and simulate `ChooseAsteroids` function for waves 1–20. Print composition, cost efficiency, and cell counts. The user then confirmed: remove countCap (redundant with cellCap), add `size_bias` for size variety, bias vector lives outside the function, and rotation/velocity belong in the procedural asteroid creation function. Proposed wave manager loop:

```
every x frames:
    if live_entities <= 30% || 30 seconds passed:
        wave_description = fetch_next_wave()
        asteroid_list = choose_asteroids(budget, cost_table, bias_vector, max_cells - live_cells)
        spawn(asteroid_list)
```

---

2. Key Technical Concepts:
- C# ECS: World, Entity, ISystem, EventBus, fixed timestep 1/120s
- Camera offset pattern: `screenPos = worldPos + camera.Offset`; `Offset = new(hw - pos.X, hh - pos.Y)`
- Frustum culling via `Camera.IsVisible(worldPos, margin)`
- VortexSystem: linear force `k × excess`, per-component velocity cap = `capFrames × force_per_frame`; soft clamp (add only what's left to reach cap)
- BorderDampSystem: per-axis exponential velocity damping; `factor = 1 - dist/zone`, `v *= exp(-DampK * factor * dt)`; only damps outward component
- Player Option A movement: WASD = world-axis, passive lateral bleed on aim-perpendicular velocity: `vPerp *= exp(-LateralDrag * fdt)` every frame regardless of input
- Wave budget system: greedy weighted-random selection; size_mult scales cost and cells proportionally; variety via per-type cap (45%, lifted for horde waves)
- ParticleSystem.Draw already takes `Vector2 offset` parameter

---

  **DemoRenderer.Draw (grid + camera offset)**:

  ```csharp
  var camera     = session.Camera;
  Vector2 camOff = camera.Offset;
  
  // World-space grid
  float wx0 = -camOff.X, wx1 = _w - camOff.X;
  float wy0 = -camOff.Y, wy1 = _h - camOff.Y;
  float gx0 = MathF.Ceiling(wx0 / GridSpacing) * GridSpacing;
  float gy0 = MathF.Ceiling(wy0 / GridSpacing) * GridSpacing;
  for (float gx = gx0; gx <= wx1; gx += GridSpacing)
      r.DrawLine(new Vector2(gx + camOff.X, 0), new Vector2(gx + camOff.X, _h), GridCol, 1f);
  for (float gy = gy0; gy <= wy1; gy += GridSpacing)
      r.DrawLine(new Vector2(0, gy + camOff.Y), new Vector2(_w, gy + camOff.Y), GridCol, 1f);
  
  // Asteroid loop: var (wpos, rot) = Interp(t, alpha); if (!camera.IsVisible(wpos, 300f)) return; var pos = wpos + camOff;
  // Debris loop: if (!camera.IsVisible(wpos, 100f)) return; var pos = wpos + camOff;

  // Bullet loop: if (!camera.IsVisible(wpos, 10f)) return; var p = wpos + camOff;
  // Player loop: var (wpos, _) = Interp(t, alpha); var p = wpos + camOff;
  // HUD: no camera offset (screen-space)
  ```

  **Option A movement** (world-axis WASD + passive lateral bleed):
  ```csharp
  var p = _gc.Player;
  ref var vel = ref world.GetComponent<Velocity>(_player);

  // Passive lateral bleed on aim-perpendicular velocity
  Vector2 fwd  = aim.Dir;
  Vector2 rgt  = new(fwd.Y, -fwd.X);
  float vAlong = Vector2.Dot(vel.Linear, fwd);
  float vPerp  = Vector2.Dot(vel.Linear, rgt);
  vPerp       *= MathF.Exp(-p.LateralDrag * fdt);
  vel.Linear   = fwd * vAlong + rgt * vPerp;

  // World-axis WASD
  Vector2 wantDir = Vector2.Zero;
  if (_input.IsHeld(KeyCode.W)) wantDir.Y -= 1;
  if (_input.IsHeld(KeyCode.S)) wantDir.Y += 1;
  if (_input.IsHeld(KeyCode.A)) wantDir.X -= 1;
  if (_input.IsHeld(KeyCode.D)) wantDir.X += 1;
  if (wantDir != Vector2.Zero) wantDir = Vector2.Normalize(wantDir);

  if (wantDir != Vector2.Zero)
  {
      bool freshPress = (_input.IsPressed(KeyCode.W) && wantDir.Y < 0)
                     || (_input.IsPressed(KeyCode.S) && wantDir.Y > 0)
                     || (_input.IsPressed(KeyCode.A) && wantDir.X < 0)
                     || (_input.IsPressed(KeyCode.D) && wantDir.X > 0);
      if (freshPress) vel.Linear += wantDir * p.Impulse;
      float step = p.Thrust * fdt;
      Vector2 target = wantDir * p.MaxSpeed;
      Vector2 diff   = target - vel.Linear;
      float diffLen  = diff.Length();
      vel.Linear += diffLen <= step ? diff : diff / diffLen * step;
      float spd = vel.Linear.Length();
      if (spd > p.MaxSpeed) vel.Linear *= p.MaxSpeed / spd;
  }
  else { vel.Linear *= MathF.Exp(-p.BrakeDrag * fdt); }
  ```

  **VortexSystem** (reads live Config params, linear formula, per-component cap):
  ```csharp
  sealed class VortexSystem : ISystem
  {
      private readonly Vector2 _centre;
      private readonly Config  _cfg;

      public VortexSystem(Vector2 centre, Config cfg) { _centre = centre; _cfg = cfg; }

      public void Update(World world, double dt)
      {
          float fdt          = (float)dt;
          float deadzone     = _cfg.VortexDeadzone.Value;
          float centripetalK = _cfg.VortexCentripetal.Value;
          float tangentialK  = _cfg.VortexTangential.Value;
          float capFrames    = _cfg.VortexCapFrames.Value;

          world.ForEach<Transform, Velocity, RigidBody>((Entity _, ref Transform t, ref Velocity v, ref RigidBody rb) =>
          {
              Vector2 toCenter = _centre - t.Position;
              float dist = toCenter.Length();
              if (dist < 1e-3f) return;
              float excess = dist - deadzone;
              if (excess <= 0f) return;

              Vector2 radial  = toCenter / dist;
              Vector2 tangent = new(-radial.Y, radial.X);

              float forceC = centripetalK * excess * fdt;
              float forceT = tangentialK  * excess * fdt;
              float capC   = forceC * capFrames;
              float capT   = forceT * capFrames;

              float vC = Vector2.Dot(v.Linear, radial);
              float vT = Vector2.Dot(v.Linear, tangent);

              if (vC < capC) v.Linear += radial  * MathF.Min(forceC, capC - vC);
              if (vT < capT) v.Linear += tangent * MathF.Min(forceT, capT - vT);
          });
      }
  }
  ```

  **BorderDampSystem** (replaced BorderBounceSystem):
  ```csharp
  sealed class BorderDampSystem : ISystem
  {
      private const float Zone  = 200f;
      private const float DampK = 20f;

      public void Update(World world, double dt)
      {
          float fdt = (float)dt;
          world.ForEach<Transform, Velocity>((Entity _, ref Transform t, ref Velocity v) =>
          {
              float x = t.Position.X, y = t.Position.Y;
              float dL = x;
              if (dL < Zone && v.Linear.X < 0f)
                  v.Linear.X *= MathF.Exp(-DampK * (1f - dL / Zone) * fdt);
              float dR = GameConst.WorldW - x;
              if (dR < Zone && v.Linear.X > 0f)
                  v.Linear.X *= MathF.Exp(-DampK * (1f - dR / Zone) * fdt);
              float dT = y;
              if (dT < Zone && v.Linear.Y < 0f)
                  v.Linear.Y *= MathF.Exp(-DampK * (1f - dT / Zone) * fdt);
              float dB = GameConst.WorldH - y;
              if (dB < Zone && v.Linear.Y > 0f)
                  v.Linear.Y *= MathF.Exp(-DampK * (1f - dB / Zone) * fdt);
              t.Position = Vector2.Clamp(t.Position, Vector2.Zero,
                  new Vector2(GameConst.WorldW, GameConst.WorldH));
          });
      }
  }
  ```

4. Errors and Fixes:
- **C# compilation: records before top-level statements**: `record AsteroidType` and `static` method declarations can't precede top-level code in C# scripts. Fixed by wrapping entire simulation in `static class Sim { static void Main() {...} }`.
- **Wave sim decimal display artifact**: `cost=  231/25` looked like integer 231. Was actually `23.1/25` with decimal invisible in terminal rendering. Fixed by changing format from `{value,5:0.1}` to `{value,6:F1}`.
- **BorderBounceSystem → BorderDampSystem rename**: The grep for `new BorderBounceSystem(),            // NEW` failed because the comment wasn't present. Fixed by running grep to find actual line and replacing correctly.
- **Stale comment header** ("BorderBounceSystem — hard bounce...") left after class rename. Fixed by replacing with updated comment.
- **Lateral movement revert**: User explicitly asked to revert ship-relative WASD (A/D strafe). Reverted to world-axis WASD. Also removed `ReverseFactor` and `LateralFactor` fields that had been added to `PlayerConfig` and `ConfigEditorDefs`.

---

5. Problem Solving:
- **Vortex runaway orbital speed**: Solved by adding per-component velocity cap (`capFrames × force_per_frame`). The cap is proportional to excess distance so objects far out can still be strongly pulled back, but the tangential spinning force never accumulates beyond what 100 frames of continuous force would produce.
- **Border bounce causing entities to fly back across the map**: Solved by replacing hard bounce with per-axis exponential velocity damping on outward component only — no counter-force applied, so entities drain to zero rather than bouncing.
- **Aim direction wrong after camera**: Fixed by converting mouse screen pos to world pos via camera offset before computing direction to ship position.
- **Ship-relative movement felt bad**: Reverted to world-axis WASD. Added passive aim-relative lateral drag to preserve directional incentive without inverting controls.
- **Wave 5 (gravel horde) budget efficiency ~70%**: Accepted — count cap fills first, which is the intended horde effect (many cheap asteroids).
- **Wave 10 asteroid count lower than design doc target**: countCap formula `8 + wave = 18` gives 8–10 asteroids at wave 10; design doc targets 20–25. Noted as potential adjustment (increase to `8 + wave*2`).

---

The vortex force constants (`centripetalK`, `tangentialK`) default to 0.10 and 0.06 with a tuner step of 0.01 — so "±5" most naturally reads as ±5 tuner steps = ±0.05 absolute. I'll add a time accumulator to `VortexSystem` and oscillate the two constants independently (11s and 13s periods, 90° offset) so they don't pulse in sync.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-15 13:05 UTC

Done. The vortex now breathes — centripetal oscillates on an 11-second cycle and tangential on a 13-second cycle (coprime so they never sync), each ±0.05 around the tuner-set base. At the tuner defaults (0.10 / 0.06), centripetal swings between 0.05–0.15 (50% variation) and tangential between 0.01–0.11. Both are clamped to ≥ 0 so they can't go negative.

If you want the variation to be more subtle, reduce the 0.05 amplitude. If you want both forces to pulse together (for a more dramatic rhythmic feel), match the two periods.

2. Key Technical Concepts:
- C# ECS: World, Entity, ISystem, EventBus, fixed timestep 1/120s
- Wave budget system: abstract cost points, per-type BaseCost/BaseCells, ChooseAsteroids packing algorithm
- Power-law size sampling: `sizeMult = minMult + u^(2^(-sizeBias)) × (maxMult - minMult)`
- Wave trigger: 30% live-cell threshold OR 30-second timer, 1.5s cooldown
- Vortex oscillation: coprime-period sine waves (11s/13s) with ±0.05 amplitude, 90° phase offset
- Voronoi tessellation: `BuildAsteroid` → `Build` → `ScatterSeeds` (GrainArea grid) → `BuildBonds` (flat strength)
- `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` fields: Roughness, NoiseFrequency, ConcavityBias, SeedCount, SeedClusterCenter, BondMultDistribution, DensityMultDistribution, BlastResistDistribution
- `AsteroidsEngine.csproj` does NOT reference GameConfig — engine classes cannot use `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` directly

  ```csharp
  _waveTimer += (float)dt;
  int liveCells = CountLiveCells();
  bool shouldSpawn = liveCells <= _maxLiveCells * 0.30f || _waveTimer >= 30f;
  if (shouldSpawn && !_pendingWave) { _pendingWave = true; _waveCountdown = 1.5f; }
  if (_pendingWave)
  {
      _waveCountdown -= (float)dt;
      if (_waveCountdown <= 0f) { SpawnNextWave(); _waveTimer = 0f; _pendingWave = false; }
  }
  ```

  ```csharp
  private int CountLiveCells()  // sums fb.Cells.Length across all AsteroidTag+FracturableBody

  private static Dictionary<string, float> DefaultBias(int wave) => new()
  { ["gravel"]=0.05f,["standard"]=0.10f,["spinner"]=0.15f,["unstable"]=0.25f,["boulder"]=0.25f,["armored"]=0.20f };

  private List<(string Key, float SizeMult)> ChooseAsteroids(
      int budget, Dictionary<string, float> bias, float sizeBias, float cellCap)
  // Packing loop: filter by unlock/bias/budget/cells, weighted pick, power-law size sample
  // alpha = MathF.Pow(2f, -sizeBias)
  // sizeMult = minMult0 + MathF.Pow(u, alpha) * (maxMult - minMult0)

  // Increments _waveNumber, grows _maxLiveCells (300 + (wave-1)*30, capped at gc.MaxLiveCells)
  // Gets waveDef from _gc.Waves, falls back to DefaultBias for waves>10
  // Calls ChooseAsteroids, then FindSpawnPosition + SpawnAsteroid for each result
  ```

  ```csharp
  // Velocity: direction toward WorldCenter ±45° spread, speed from ac.SpeedRange
  // float baseAngle = MathF.Atan2(toCenter.Y, toCenter.X);
  // float spread = ((float)_rng.NextDouble() * 2f - 1f) * (MathF.PI / 4f);

  ```

  ```csharp
  public void Respawn()
  {
      foreach (var e in new List<Entity>(_world.QueryEntities<AsteroidTag>())) _world.DestroyEntity(e);
      _pendingWave = false;
      // reset player to WorldCenter + zero velocity
      SpawnNextWave();
      _waveTimer = 0f;
  }
  ```

  ```csharp
  sealed class VortexSystem : ISystem
  {
      private readonly Vector2 _centre;
      private readonly Config  _cfg;
      private float _time = 0f;   // NEW

      public void Update(World world, double dt)
      {
          float fdt = (float)dt;
          _time += fdt;   // NEW
          float deadzone     = _cfg.VortexDeadzone.Value;
          // NEW: ±0.05 oscillation on 11s and 13s coprime periods, 90° phase offset
          float centripetalK = MathF.Max(0f, _cfg.VortexCentripetal.Value
                               + 0.05f * MathF.Sin(_time * MathF.Tau / 11f));
          float tangentialK  = MathF.Max(0f, _cfg.VortexTangential.Value
                               + 0.05f * MathF.Sin(_time * MathF.Tau / 13f + MathF.PI * 0.5f));
          ...
      }
  }
  ```

5. Problem Solving:

**Wave system**: Designed and implemented stateless `ChooseAsteroids` packing algorithm with power-law size bias. The key insight: `SizeRange` in `AsteroidConfig` already IS the size_mult range — no separate field needed. Wave 5 (gravel horde) correctly produces 22-34 tiny asteroids; wave 3 (boulder) produces 4-6 large boulders.

**Vortex oscillation**: Interpreted user's "±5" as ±5 tuner steps = ±0.05 absolute. Used coprime periods (11s, 13s) to avoid synchronization. MathF.Max(0f, ...) prevents negative force constants.

**Procedural asteroid gap analysis** (ongoing, not yet fixed):
- 7 out of 9 `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` parameters are completely unused
- Most gameplay-impactful: `BondMultDistribution` (boulder tough core / armored tough surface), `BlastResistDistribution` (armored blast immunity at surface)
- `Cell` struct lacks `DensityMult` and `BlastResist` fields — required additions
- Engine/GameConfig separation constraint: fix needs a parameter struct in engine namespace or caller-side translation

**What `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` declares vs what `BuildAsteroid` uses:**
- `BaseRadius` ✓ USED
- `VertexCount[0..1]` ✓ USED (for `sides` parameter)
- `Roughness` ✗ NOT USED — `GenerateConvex` uses hardcoded `radiusVariation=0.22f`
- `NoiseFrequency` ✗ NOT USED
- `ConcavityBias` ✗ NOT USED — always passes `membership: null`
- `SeedCount[0..1]` ✗ NOT USED — seeds from GrainArea grid
- `SeedClusterCenter` ✗ NOT USED
- `BondMultDistribution` ✗ NOT USED — `Build` uses `BuildBonds` (flat), not `BuildBondsWeighted`
- `DensityMultDistribution` ✗ NOT USED — Cell has no DensityMult field
- `BlastResistDistribution` ✗ NOT USED — Cell has no BlastResist field

**Critical architectural constraint discovered:** `AsteroidsEngine.csproj` does NOT reference `GameConfig` project. Therefore `VoronoiTessellator.cs` cannot import `ProceduralAsteroidConfig`. The fix approach must define a parameter struct inside the engine, and have `SpawnAsteroid` in `Program.cs` translate from `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` → engine struct before calling the tessellator.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-15 15:01 UTC

Zero warnings, zero errors. Here's a summary of what was fixed and how it maps to the config fields:

| Config field | Fix |
|---|---|
| `Roughness` + `NoiseFrequency` | `BuildProceduralAsteroid` applies sinusoidal noise to vertex radii (outward only to preserve convexity) |
| `ConcavityBias` | Membership predicate: probability of dropping a cell ∝ `bias × r²` (more likely at the surface) |
| `SeedCount` + `SeedClusterCenter` | `ScatterSeedsProc`: explicit seed count from config, radial power distribution biases toward centroid |
| `BondMultDistribution` | `EvalProcDist` called per seed → passed as `seedBondMults` to new `BuildWithSeeds`; geometric-mean weighting already in `BuildBondsWeighted` |
| `DensityMultDistribution` | `EvalProcDist` per cell centroid → patches `Cell.DensityMult` post-build |
| `BlastResistDistribution` | `EvalProcDist` per cell centroid → patches `Cell.BlastResist` post-build |

Engine-level fixes:
- `Cell` now carries `DensityMult` (default 1) and `BlastResist` (default 0) — backwards-compatible
- `VoronoiTessellator.TotalMass` computes density-weighted mass; `SpawnBody` now uses it
- `ComputeInertia` is density-weighted so boulders with dense cores get correct rotational inertia
- `FractureSimulator` blast threshold uses per-cell `BlastResist` — armored asteroid surface cells require much more energy to vaporize
- Fragment rebuild copies `DensityMult`/`BlastResist` so properties survive fragmentation

Clean. Summary of all changes:

**Screen size** — `SdlGameWindow.QueryDisplaySize()` calls `SDL_GetCurrentDisplayMode(0)` before window creation. Program.cs now uses this for `W`/`H`, and the window is created with `SDL_WINDOW_FULLSCREEN_DESKTOP` so it covers the full display without a mode change.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-16 21:50 UTC

Agreed on all points. Here's my take on point 2:

The original `Build()` path already does this correctly — `ScatterSeeds` computes `step = sqrt(GrainArea)` and fills the bounding box on a jittered grid, so seed count falls out of `asteroidArea / GrainArea` automatically. The bug I introduced was `BuildProceduralAsteroid` bypassing that with an explicit `SeedCount`.

**Proposed design:**
- Remove `SeedCount[]` from `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` and `game_config.json`
- In `BuildProceduralAsteroid`, derive seed count from `(π × radius²) / mat.GrainArea`, clamped to e.g. `[4, 600]`
- Keep `SeedClusterCenter` — it controls spatial distribution (not count), and is legitimately a per-asteroid-type parameter
- Keep `BaseCells` in `AsteroidConfig` as the wave manager's single rough estimate. You tune GrainArea per material to drive actual density; you tune `BaseCells` to tell the wave manager how expensive that asteroid type is

The only subtle consequence: with area-based seeding, a sizeMult=2 asteroid has ~4× more cells than sizeMult=1 (area scales as r²). The wave manager's `BaseCells × sizeMult` is a linear approximation of that — slightly wrong but close enough for rough budgeting, which is fine given point 3.

Does this match your intent, or would you prefer something different before I implement?

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-16 21:57 UTC

I don't see any reason to keep baseCells. If I change the material cell granularity the baseCells wouldn't reflect that and the Wave manager would make decisions based on a stale value. baseCells should either be derived (just as seedcount is) at the beginning or completely removed. Also the linear vs quadratic approximation isn't acceptable since the size can have pretty big ranges and it could accumulate errors pretty fast.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-16 21:57 UTC

Completely agree. The derived formula `π × (BaseRadius × sizeMult)² / GrainArea` is the single truth — changing GrainArea immediately affects both actual seed count and the wave manager's cost estimate without any manual sync.

**Implementation plan:**
- Remove `BaseCells` from `AsteroidConfig` + `game_config.json`
- Remove `SeedCount` from `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` + `game_config.json`
- Add `CellsFor(ac, sizeMult)` helper in `DemoSession` that computes `π × (BaseRadius × sizeMult)² / GrainArea`
- `ChooseAsteroids`: filter on `CellsFor(ac, minMult)`, invert the quadratic for `maxByCells` → `mult ≤ sqrt(remCells × GrainArea / (π × BaseRadius²))`, deduct `CellsFor(chosenAc, sizeMult)`
- `BuildProceduralAsteroid`: `seedCount = clamp(π × radius² / GrainArea, 4, 600)`
- `LogAndBannerWave`: use `CellsFor` for estimates

### Task 2 — Per-entity vortex response

**One clarifying question first:** you said "The cap should also be multiplied" alongside "2 coefficients." I want to confirm: is `DeadzoneMult` a 3rd independent coefficient on the `VortexResponse` component, or does the deadzone scale with one of the force coefficients (e.g., the cap shrinks when centripetal is negative, meaning the entity is pulled to center instead)?

My assumption for the plan: **3 fields on the component** — `CentripetalMult`, `TangentialMult`, `DeadzoneMult` — all per-entity, all independent.

**New component (engine layer):**
```csharp
public struct VortexResponse
{
    public float CentripetalMult;  // <0 = pushed away from center
    public float TangentialMult;   // <0 = reversed spin
    public float DeadzoneMult;     // scales the global deadzone radius
}
```

**Config-side (per asteroid type in game_config):**
```json
"vortexResponse": {
    "centripetalRange": [0.5, 2.0],
    "tangentialRange":  [0.3, 1.5],
    "deadzoneRange":    [0.8, 1.2]
}
```

**Player** gets fixed values in `"player"` section: `"vortexCentripetal": 0.5, "vortexTangential": 0.5, "vortexDeadzone": 1.0`.

**VortexSystem change:** query entities that have both `Velocity/RigidBody` and `VortexResponse`; use the per-entity multipliers. Entities without the component are unaffected (or we could give everything a default — but explicit opt-in is cleaner given "future things").

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-17 11:00 UTC

Updated plan:

---

## Sprint — revised

### Task 1 — game_config single source of truth
*(unchanged from before)*

---

### Task 2 — Per-entity vortex response

**Clarification accepted:** `VortexResponse` has 2 force multipliers. The velocity cap is also multiplied — one open question: is the cap a **3rd independent field** in `VortexResponse` (so you can configure "this asteroid is hard to deflect but moves a lot"), or does it **derive from the force multipliers** (e.g., scales with `max(|CentripetalMult|, |TangentialMult|)` implicitly)?

My recommendation: keep it a 3rd explicit field. Deriving it implicitly loses configurability — a rock with high tangential but low centripetal mult would get a cap driven by the wrong axis. So:

```csharp
public struct VortexResponse
{
    public float CentripetalMult;
    public float TangentialMult;
    public float CapMult;
}
```

Config range per asteroid type:
```json
"vortexResponse": {
    "centripetalRange": [-0.5, 2.0],
    "tangentialRange":  [0.2,  1.5],
    "capRange":         [0.5,  1.5]
}
```

Only entities with `VortexResponse` are affected — explicit opt-in.

---

### Task 3 — Direct value typing in the editor

Each slider in the game editor gets a text input. Typing a value sets it immediately. Typing a new **min** or **max** at the range boundaries re-scales the slider to fit. So the slider range is runtime-mutable per parameter, not baked into the definition.

This needs changes to the editor's slider widget and the underlying `EditorDef` / `Tunable` infrastructure. I'll need to look at that code before estimating scope.

---

**One question before I start**: does the VortexResponse config range go on the asteroid type (`ProceduralAsteroidConfig`/`AsteroidConfig`) or on the material? I'd put it on the asteroid type since it's a gameplay behavior property, not a physical material property — but want to confirm.

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-17 11:05 UTC

<ide_selection>The user selected the lines 1574 to 1584 from /home/sebastian/ADVANCED/workspace/GameEngine/Demos/AsteroidDemo/Program.cs:

            // Per-component velocity cap: capFrames × one frame of force at this excess.
            // Projections are positive when velocity already agrees with the force direction.
            // The cap only kicks in when velocity and force are co-directional — if an object
            // is moving outward (against centripetal) or CW (against tangential) the full force
            // is always applied. The soft clamp adds only what's left to reach the cap,
            // removing the discontinuity at the threshold.
            float forceC = centripetalK * excess * fdt;
            float forceT = tangentialK * excess * fdt;
            float capC = forceC * capFrames;
            float capT = forceT * capFrames;

This may or may not be related to the current task.</ide_selection>
Actually, the capFrames as it is implemented right now would already be affected by the coefficient since they multiply forceC and forceT, which will be multiplied by the coefficient so there's no need for any new variable. 
The VortexResponse goes on the asteroid type.

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:

This session continued "Asteroids on Steroids" — a C# 2D physics/destruction arcade game. Major work completed in order:

**A. Fix procedural asteroid creation** — 7/9 `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` fields were completely unused. Fixed all: Roughness/NoiseFrequency (outline noise), ConcavityBias (membership predicate), SeedCount/SeedClusterCenter (explicit seed scatter), BondMultDistribution (per-seed bond strength), DensityMultDistribution and BlastResistDistribution (per-cell properties). Required adding `DensityMult`/`BlastResist` to `Cell` struct.

**B. HUD features** — (1) live cell counter at bottom of screen, (2) wave spawn pop-up banner with fade, (3) `wave_spawns.log` file written every wave with full asteroid breakdown.

**C. Screen size + wave bugs** — Window hardcoded to 1920×1080; fixed by querying SDL display size. Wave double-trigger bug (small wave → `_liveCells` still ≤ 30% threshold on next frame, immediately queuing wave 2). Early-return path in `SpawnNextWave` skipped logging.

**D. Cell count single source of truth** — Wave manager used `BaseCells × sizeMult` (wrong, linear). Actual cells come from `π × (BaseRadius × sizeMult)² / GrainArea`. Decision: remove both `BaseCells` from `AsteroidConfig` AND `SeedCount[]` from `ProceduralAsteroidConfig`. Single formula everywhere: `CellsFor(ac, sizeMult)` in wave manager; `clamp(π × r² / GrainArea, 4, 600)` in `BuildProceduralAsteroid`. `ChooseAsteroids` now uses quadratic inversion for the cell cap constraint.

**E. Sprint planning (current)** — Three tasks defined for next sprint:
1. game_config as single source of truth — remove `Config`/`Tunable` system, move all meaningful parameters to game_config
2. `VortexResponse` component — per-entity coefficients (CentripetalMult, TangentialMult) multiplying vortex forces; the velocity frame-cap is also multiplied per entity; only entities with the component are affected; player gets (0.5, 0.5); asteroid types have ranges in config; negative coefficients allowed (go against current)
3. Direct value typing in editor — text input per parameter; slider range adapts to typed min/max

---

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- C# ECS: World, Entity, ISystem, EventBus, fixed timestep 1/120s
- Voronoi tessellation for asteroid fracture bodies (`VoronoiTessellator`)
- `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` fields: Roughness, NoiseFrequency, ConcavityBias, SeedClusterCenter, BondMultDistribution, DensityMultDistribution, BlastResistDistribution
- `CellPropertyDistribution` types: "constant", "radialGradient", "noiseClusters"
- Per-cell `DensityMult` (mass weighting) and `BlastResist` (blast threshold scaling)
- `BuildWithSeeds`: tessellates with explicit seeds + membership predicate + weighted bonds
- Wave budget system: abstract cost (BaseCost × sizeMult), cell cap derived from GrainArea formula
- Cell cap formula: `π × (BaseRadius × sizeMult)² / GrainArea` — single source of truth
- Quadratic inversion for maxByCells: `mult ≤ sqrt(remCells / CellsFor(ac, 1))`
- Vortex oscillation: coprime periods (11s/13s), ±0.05 amplitude on centripetal/tangential
- SDL `QueryDisplaySize` + `WindowFlags.FullscreenDesktop` for display-native resolution
- `AsteroidsEngine.csproj` does NOT reference `GameConfig` — engine classes cannot use config types directly
- C# struct field initializers require explicit parameterless constructor (CS8983)

3. Files and Code Sections:

- **`GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/Cell.cs`**

  ```csharp
  public struct Cell
  {
      public Vector2[] Local = null!;
      public Vector2   Centroid;
      public float     Area;
      public float     DensityMult = 1f;
      public float     BlastResist = 0f;
      public Cell() { }
  ```

- **`GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/VoronoiTessellator.cs`**
  - Added `BuildWithSeeds(convexBound, seedPositions, seedBondMults, membership, material, rng)`: full Voronoi over all seeds, drops cells failing membership after tessellation (holes preserved), uses `BuildBondsWeighted`
  - Added `TotalMass(body)`: density-weighted mass = `max(1, Density × Σ(cell.Area × cell.DensityMult))`
  - Updated `ComputeInertia` to use `cell.Area × cell.DensityMult` weighting instead of `cell.Area`
  ```csharp
  public static float TotalMass(in FracturableBody body)
  {
      float weighted = 0f;
      foreach (var c in body.Cells) weighted += c.Area * c.DensityMult;
      return MathF.Max(1f, body.Material.Density * weighted);
  }
  ```

- **`GameEngine/Engine/Destruction/FractureSimulator.cs`**
  - Line 333 fragment rebuild: added `DensityMult = src.DensityMult, BlastResist = src.BlastResist` to cell copy
  - Blast threshold: replaced flat `blastBase` with per-cell: `cellThresh = blastBase + cells[i].BlastResist × (EnergyTotal - blastBase)`
  ```csharp
  float blastBase = (1f - blast) * input.EnergyTotal;
  for (int i = 0; i < cells.Length; i++)
  {
      if (energy[i] <= 0f) continue;
      float cellThresh = blastBase + cells[i].BlastResist * (input.EnergyTotal - blastBase);
      if (energy[i] > cellThresh) pulverized[i] = true;
  }
  ```

  ```csharp
  private float _gameTime  = 0f;
  ```

  ```csharp
  bool shouldSpawn = (_liveCells <= _maxLiveCells * 0.30f && _waveTimer > 8f)
                  || _waveTimer >= 30f;
  ```

  *CellsFor helper (single source of truth):*
  ```csharp
  private float CellsFor(AsteroidConfig ac, float sizeMult)
  {
      if (ac.Procedural == null) return 1f;
      if (!_gc.Materials.TryGetValue(ac.Material, out var mc)) return 1f;
      float r = ac.Procedural.BaseRadius * sizeMult;
      return MathF.Max(1f, MathF.PI * r * r / mc.GrainArea);
  }
  ```

  *ChooseAsteroids with quadratic cell cap:*
  ```csharp
  if (CellsFor(ac, minMult) > remCells) continue;
  // ...
  float kUnit = CellsFor(chosenAc, 1f);
  float maxByCells = MathF.Sqrt(remCells / kUnit);
  float maxMult = Math.Min(chosenAc.SizeRange[1], Math.Min(maxByBudget, maxByCells));
  // ...
  remCells -= CellsFor(chosenAc, sizeMult);
  ```

  *BuildProceduralAsteroid seed count (GrainArea-derived):*
  ```csharp
  int seedCount = Math.Clamp((int)(MathF.PI * radius * radius / mat.GrainArea), 4, 600);
  ```

  *LogAndBannerWave: uses CellsFor instead of BaseCells*

  *SpawnAsteroid: replaced VoronoiTessellator.BuildAsteroid with BuildProceduralAsteroid call*

  *SpawnBody: uses VoronoiTessellator.TotalMass(body) instead of Density × area*

  *Full BuildProceduralAsteroid implementation:*
  1. Generates convex outline via `PolygonUtils.GenerateConvex`
  2. Applies roughness noise (outward only to preserve convexity)
  3. Seeds derived from `π × radius² / GrainArea`
  4. Per-seed bond mults from `BondMultDistribution` via `EvalProcDist`
  5. Concavity membership: `prob = ConcavityBias × r²`
  6. `VoronoiTessellator.BuildWithSeeds(convex, seeds, bondMults, membership, mat, _rng)`
  7. Post-build: patches `DensityMult` and `BlastResist` per cell from distributions

  *EvalProcDist:*
  ```csharp
  private static float EvalProcDist(CellPropertyDistribution? dist, Vector2 pos, float maxR)
  {
      if (dist == null) return 1f;
      float r = maxR > 0f ? Math.Clamp(pos.Length() / maxR, 0f, 1f) : 0f;
      return dist.Type switch
      {
          "radialGradient" =>
              (dist.CenterValue  ?? 1f) * (1f - MathF.Pow(r, dist.Exponent ?? 1f))
            + (dist.SurfaceValue ?? 1f) *       MathF.Pow(r, dist.Exponent ?? 1f),
          "noiseClusters" =>
              Math.Clamp(
                  (dist.BaseValue ?? 1f) + (dist.Amplitude ?? 0f) *
                  (MathF.Sin(pos.X * (dist.Frequency ?? 1f) / maxR * MathF.Tau + 1.73f)
                 * MathF.Cos(pos.Y * (dist.Frequency ?? 1f) / maxR * MathF.Tau + 0.91f)),
                  0f, 10f),
          _ => dist.Value,
      };
  }
  ```

- **`GameEngine/Platform/Sdl/SdlGameWindow.cs`**
  - Added `QueryDisplaySize(int displayIndex = 0)` static method using `SDL_GetCurrentDisplayMode`
  - Added `bool fullscreen = false` constructor parameter
  - Uses `WindowFlags.FullscreenDesktop` when fullscreen = true
  - Override width/height from display mode when fullscreen
  ```csharp
  public static (int Width, int Height) QueryDisplaySize(int displayIndex = 0)
  {
      var sdl = SdlApi.GetApi();
      sdl.Init(SdlApi.InitVideo);
      DisplayMode mode = default;
      sdl.GetCurrentDisplayMode(displayIndex, ref mode);
      return (mode.W > 0 ? mode.W : 1920, mode.H > 0 ? mode.H : 1080);
  }
  ```

- **`GameEngine/Demos/AsteroidDemo/ConfigEditorDefs.cs`**
  - Removed "Seeds Min" and "Seeds Max" `SliderInt` entries (referenced removed `SeedCount` property)

---

4. Errors and Fixes:

- **CS8983: struct with field initializers must have explicit constructor**
  - `Cell.cs` had `DensityMult = 1f` and `BlastResist = 0f` field initializers
  - Fix: added `public Cell() { }` parameterless constructor
  - Also added `= null!` to `Local` field to suppress CS8618 nullable warning

- **Stale file state on Edit tool**
  - Python regex replacement used instead when Edit tool reported stale file
  - Pattern: `python3 -c "content = open(...).read(); content = content.replace(old, new, 1); open(..., 'w').write(content)"`

- **ConfigEditorDefs.cs referencing removed `SeedCount` property**
  - Build error: `CS1061: 'ProceduralAsteroidConfig' does not contain a definition for 'SeedCount'`
  - Fix: removed the two `SliderInt` lines for "Seeds Min" and "Seeds Max" in `ConfigEditorDefs.cs`

- **Wave double-trigger bug**
  - Right after wave spawn, `_liveCells` could still be ≤ 30% threshold (small first wave → few cells)
  - This caused wave 2 to queue on the very next frame
  - Fix: added `&& _waveTimer > 8f` guard: threshold can only trigger after 8s have elapsed since last wave

- **Early-return path skipped logging**
  - When `cellCap < 3f`, `SpawnNextWave` returned before `LogAndBannerWave`
  - Fix: call `LogAndBannerWave(waveDef, new List<(string Key, float SizeMult)>(), budget, sizeBias)` before return

- **User corrupted Program.cs mid-edit**
  - OmniSharp conflict markers appeared in the file
  - User reverted to previous state; work continued from reverted state

---

5. Problem Solving:

- **Architectural constraint**: `AsteroidsEngine.csproj` does NOT reference `GameConfig`. Solution: demo-layer (`Program.cs`) bridges between the two — `BuildProceduralAsteroid` in `DemoSession` translates `ProceduralAsteroidConfig` into engine calls.

- **Cell count inconsistency**: `BaseCells × sizeMult` (linear, hand-tuned) vs. actual Voronoi cells from `SeedCount` (fixed per type). Resolution: remove both explicit fields; derive from `π × r² / GrainArea` everywhere. ChooseAsteroids uses quadratic inversion: `maxMult ≤ sqrt(remCells / CellsFor(ac, 1))`.

- **SeedClusterCenter preservation**: Even though `SeedCount` was removed, `SeedClusterCenter` was kept — it controls spatial distribution of seeds, not count, and is legitimately a per-asteroid-type parameter.

---

  ```csharp
  public struct VortexResponse
  {
      public float CentripetalMult; // <0 = pushed outward instead of inward
      public float TangentialMult;  // <0 = reversed spin direction
      public float CapMult;         // multiplies the per-frame velocity cap
  }
  ```
- Add vortex response range to asteroid type config in game_config per asteroid type:
  ```json
  "vortexResponse": {
      "centripetalRange": [0.5, 2.0],
      "tangentialRange":  [0.3, 1.5],
      "capRange":         [0.8, 1.2]
  }
  ```

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-17 11:25 UTC

Isn't there a way to add to the engine World.ForEach overloads for a variable amount of type arguments?

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-17 11:25 UTC

C# doesn't have variadic generic type parameters, so there's no compile-time way to generate them. The standard approach (what Unity DOTS, Arch ECS, etc. all do) is to add the overloads manually up to whatever arity you need — it's pure copy-paste of the same pattern. Adding `T4` takes about 10 lines in each of the two files.

Let me add the 4-argument overloads now:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-17 11:25 UTC

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-17 11:26 UTC

Now update `VortexSystem` to use the clean 4-arg overload:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-17 11:26 UTC

Clean build. C# doesn't have variadic generics, so the manual approach is the only way — but it's purely mechanical: each new arity adds one delegate in [QueryResults.cs](GameEngine/Engine/Core/QueryResults.cs) and two methods in [World.cs](GameEngine/Engine/Core/World.cs) following the exact same pattern. You now have overloads up to T4. When you need T5 (e.g. another system matching 5 components), the expansion is obvious.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:

This session implemented three sprint tasks for "Asteroids on Steroids" (C# 2D destruction arcade game):

**Task 1 — game_config as single source of truth:** Remove the old `Config`/`Tunable`/`TunableApplySystem` system entirely. Move all hardcoded or tuner-only parameters (vortex, vfx, fracture timing, physics) into `game_config.json` as new sections with corresponding C# model classes. All `_cfg.*` reads throughout the codebase replaced with `_gc.*`.

**Task 2 — VortexResponse component:** New per-entity ECS component with `CentripetalMult` and `TangentialMult` fields. Only entities with this component are affected by the vortex. Multipliers are sampled from per-asteroid-type ranges in game_config at spawn. Player gets fixed `(0.5, 0.5)`. Fragments inherit parent's VortexResponse. No separate `CapMult` field needed — the cap derives from `forceC * capFrames`, and since forceC is already multiplied by `CentripetalMult`, the cap scales automatically (confirmed by user observing the code).

**Task 3 — Direct value typing in editor:** Each slider's value display area becomes a clickable inline text input. Click the number, type a value, press Enter to apply (clamped to existing [min, max]). The slider range does NOT need to adapt (user explicitly confirmed: "The slider adaptation isn't necessary"). In progress at time of summary.

**World.ForEach 4-arg overload:** User asked "Isn't there a way to add to the engine World.ForEach overloads for a variable amount of type arguments?" — explained C# has no variadic generics, so manual overloads per arity is the standard (Unity DOTS pattern), then added the T4 overloads.

---

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- C# ECS: World, Entity, ISystem, EventBus, fixed timestep 1/120s
- `World.ForEach<T1,T2,T3,T4>` — manual arity overloads (C# has no variadic generics)
- `EcsAction<T1,T2,T3,T4>` delegate type
- `VortexResponse` — new engine component struct, opt-in per entity
- `VortexConfig`, `VfxConfig`, `FractureGlobalConfig`, `PhysicsConfig` — new GameConfig model classes
- `VortexResponseConfig` — per-asteroid-type ranges for sampling VortexResponse at spawn
- `SampleVortexResponse(AsteroidConfig, Random)` — helper that samples from `VortexResponseConfig`
- Fragment VortexResponse inheritance — parent's component read before `DestroyEntity`, passed to `SpawnBody`
- `SdlSymToChar` — maps SDL keysyms to printable chars; `.` (46) was missing, needed for numeric text input
- Immediate-mode UI (`Ui.cs`) — `_focusedInputId`, `_inputBuffer`, `_cursorPos` for text input state
- `EditorDef<T>` — declarative editor bindings via expression trees

---

3. Files and Code Sections:

- **`GameEngine/GameConfig/Models/VortexConfig.cs`** — NEW. Vortex system parameters (Deadzone, Centripetal, Tangential, CapFrames, VariationCentripetal, VariationTangential).

- **`GameEngine/GameConfig/Models/FractureGlobalConfig.cs`** — NEW. Global fracture timing and collision parameters (CrackSteps, CrackFrames, DetachOnSplit, AsteroidEnergyScale, AsteroidBlastFraction, AsteroidDirSpin, BulletMass, EnergyScale).

- **`GameEngine/GameConfig/Models/PhysicsConfig.cs`** — NEW. Default asteroid physics (LinearDrag, AngularDrag, Restitution, Friction).

  ```csharp
  public struct VortexResponse
  {
      public float CentripetalMult;
      public float TangentialMult;
  }
  ```

  - standard: `{"centripetalRange":[0.6,1.4],"tangentialRange":[0.5,1.5]}`
  - spinner: `{"centripetalRange":[0.3,1.2],"tangentialRange":[1.0,2.5]}`
  - boulder: `{"centripetalRange":[0.4,1.0],"tangentialRange":[0.2,0.8]}`
  - armored: `{"centripetalRange":[-0.5,0.5],"tangentialRange":[-0.5,0.5]}`

- **`GameEngine/Engine/Core/QueryResults.cs`** — Added 4-arg delegate:
  ```csharp
  public delegate void EcsAction<T1, T2, T3, T4>(Entity e, ref T1 c1, ref T2 c2, ref T3 c3, ref T4 c4)
      where T1 : struct where T2 : struct where T3 : struct where T4 : struct;
  ```

- **`GameEngine/Engine/Core/World.cs`** — Added `ForEach<T1,T2,T3,T4>` and `ForEachParallel<T1,T2,T3,T4>` overloads following the same dense-index pattern as the T1/T2/T3 variants. `ForEach` iterates over s1 (the smallest/first store) and filters by `!s2.Has(id) || !s3.Has(id) || !s4.Has(id)`.

- **`GameEngine/Demos/AsteroidDemo/Tuner.cs`** — DELETED. Contained `Param`, `Tuner`, and `Config` classes. All functionality removed.

- **`GameEngine/Demos/AsteroidDemo/Program.cs`** — Major refactor:
  - Removed `var cfg = new Config()`, `bool showPanel`, arrow key tuning, M key
  - `DemoSession` constructor signature: `(int, int, InputSystem, GameConfig, Dictionary<string,ShapeData>)` — `Config` removed
  - `SpawnBody` signature: added `VortexResponse? vortexResponse = null` parameter; uses `_gc.Physics.*`
  - `SpawnAsteroid(pos, typeKey, sizeMult)`: adds `SampleVortexResponse` call, passes to `SpawnBody`
  - `SpawnPlayer`: adds VortexResponse from `_gc.Player.VortexCentripetal/VortexTangential`
  - Fragment spawn (`OnFractureCompleted`, `OnFractureSplit`): reads parent VortexResponse, passes to SpawnBody
  - `OnBulletHit`: uses `_gc.Fracture.BulletMass * _gc.Fracture.EnergyScale`
  - `OnCollision`: uses `_gc.Fracture.*` throughout
  - `EmitFlash`, `EmitDustBurst`: use `_gc.Vfx.*`
  - `SpawnCellDebris`: uses `DebrisTtl`/`DebrisScatter` properties
  - Added convenience properties: `private float DebrisTtl => _gc.Vfx.DebrisTtl;` and `DebrisScatter`
  - Added `SampleVortexResponse(AsteroidConfig ac, Random rng)` helper
  - `PlayerControlSystem`: removed `Config _cfg`, fallback values now hardcoded
  - `VortexSystem`: takes `VortexConfig` instead of `Config`; uses `world.ForEach<Transform,Velocity,RigidBody,VortexResponse>` with 4-arg overload; multipliers applied per-entity
  - `TunableApplySystem` class: DELETED
  - `DemoRenderer.Draw`: signature `(IRenderer, DemoSession, GameConfig gc, float alpha, float fps)`; tracer from `gc.Vfx`; no DrawPanel; updated help text
  - Renderer no longer calls `DrawPanel`; `DrawPanel` method deleted

- **`GameEngine/Platform/Sdl/SdlGameWindow.cs`** — Added `46 => '.'` to `SdlSymToChar`:
  ```csharp
  private static char SdlSymToChar(int sym) => sym switch
  {
      >= 97 and <= 122 => (char)sym,
      >= 48 and <= 57  => (char)sym,
      95               => '_',
      45               => '-',
      46               => '.',   // ← added
      32               => ' ',
      _                => '\0'
  };
  ```

- **`GameEngine/Engine/Ui/Ui.cs`** — Read in full. `Slider` currently draws value as static text at `tx + tw + 4f` in `ColTextDim`. `TextInput` uses `_focusedInputId`/`_inputBuffer`/`_cursorPos` for inline text editing. Layout constants: `LabelW=148f`, `ValW=56f`, `RowH=24f`, `Pad=8f`.

---

4. Errors and Fixes:

- **CS0305: `World.ForEach<T>` requires 1 type argument** — VortexSystem used a 4-arg ForEach but only T1/T2/T3 overloads existed. Initially worked around with `ForEach<T1,T2,T3>` + `HasComponent` check inside. Then user asked about variadic generics → explained C# doesn't have them → added proper T4 overloads to `QueryResults.cs` and `World.cs`, then switched VortexSystem back to the clean 4-arg form.

- **Initial VortexSystem with `HasComponent` workaround** (before T4 overload added):
  ```csharp
  world.ForEach<Transform, Velocity, RigidBody>(
      (Entity e, ref Transform t, ref Velocity v, ref RigidBody rb) =>
  {
      if (!world.HasComponent<VortexResponse>(e)) return;
      ref var vr = ref world.GetComponent<VortexResponse>(e);
      ...
  });
  ```
  Replaced with clean 4-arg version after adding the overload.

---

5. Problem Solving:

- **C# variadic generics:** C# doesn't have them (unlike C++ template packs). The solution is manually adding overloads per arity — the same approach Unity DOTS, Arch ECS, and other C# ECS frameworks use. Added T4 overloads to both `QueryResults.cs` and `World.cs`.

- **Fragment VortexResponse inheritance:** When an asteroid fractures, fragments should keep the same vortex behavior as the parent. Solution: read `HasComponent<VortexResponse>` on the parent entity before `DestroyEntity`, pass it as optional parameter to `SpawnBody` for each fragment. Default is `(1f, 1f)` if parent has no component.

- **Cap scaling:** User confirmed the velocity cap (capFrames × forceC) automatically scales with the per-entity multiplier because forceC already has the multiplier applied, so no separate `CapMult` field in `VortexResponse` is needed.

---

A separate slider text-input ID is formed as `id | 0x8000_0000_0000_0000UL` to avoid collision with slider drag IDs. When Enter is pressed while focused, `float.TryParse` with `NumberStyles.Float` and `CultureInfo.InvariantCulture` is used to parse, then `Math.Clamp(parsed, min, max)` is applied. `SliderInt` automatically benefits since it delegates to `Slider` and then rounds.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 07:06 UTC

Now I have a complete picture. Here's a clear breakdown:

---

## Config Source

Yes — both the game and the demo read the same `Assets/game_config.json`. The issue is PlayingState **ignores several sections** that the demo reads.

---

## Confirmed Bugs in PlayingState

### 1. Ship doesn't rotate — `t.Rotation` is never set
`PlayerControlSystem` updates `aim.Dir` to point at the mouse but **never writes it back to `Transform.Rotation`**. The demo does this at line 1339:
```csharp
t.Rotation = MathF.Atan2(aim.Dir.Y, aim.Dir.X) + MathF.PI / 2f;
```
This single missing line is why the ship visually doesn't rotate.

### 2. Movement model is wrong
The demo uses a **direct velocity model** driven by `MaxSpeed`, `BrakeDrag`, `LateralDrag`, `Impulse`, and `RotSpeed` — all in `PlayerConfig`. PlayingState instead calls `PhysicsSystem.ApplyForce`, which only pushes a force and relies on `LinearDrag` to cap speed. Result: no max speed, no brake on key release, no lateral bleed, sluggish feel. The four `PlayerConfig` fields (`MaxSpeed`, `BrakeDrag`, `LateralDrag`, `Impulse`) are defined but **never read** in PlayingState.

### 3. Aim rotation is instant, not rate-limited
The demo smoothly rotates toward the mouse at `RotSpeed` rad/s. PlayingState snaps `aim.Dir` directly to the mouse position — also never using `RotSpeed` from config.

---

## Config Sections Used vs. Ignored

| Section | Demo | PlayingState |
|---|---|---|
| `player` (MaxSpeed, BrakeDrag, etc.) | ✅ all fields | ❌ Thrust only; MaxSpeed/BrakeDrag/LateralDrag/Impulse/RotSpeed unused |
| `vfx` | ✅ all fields | ❌ entirely hardcoded |
| `fracture` | ✅ BulletMass, EnergyScale, etc. | ✅ (via weapon configs) |
| `physics` | ✅ LinearDrag, AngularDrag for asteroids | ❌ hardcoded `0.05f` at spawn |
| `vortex` | ✅ + per-entity `VortexResponse` | ✅ global only, no VortexResponse |

---

## Other Missing Things

- **No background grid** — demo draws a world-space grid at 200px spacing; PlayingState renders a solid black background only
- **No per-entity VortexResponse** — PlayingState's `VortexSystem` uses the global config but ignores the `VortexResponse` component we added (all asteroids behave identically)
- **Asteroid physics hardcoded** — `LinearDrag = 0.05f` at line 751 instead of `ctx.Config.Physics.LinearDrag`

---

Want me to fix all of these now? The movement model replacement and the rotation line are the highest priority since they make the game unplayable.

  **VortexResponse spawning** — added `SampleVortexResponse(AsteroidConfig ac)` helper matching demo exactly:
  ```csharp
  private VortexResponse SampleVortexResponse(AsteroidConfig ac)
  {
      var vc = ac.VortexResponse;
      if (vc == null) return new VortexResponse { CentripetalMult = 1f, TangentialMult = 1f };
      float c = vc.CentripetalRange[0] + (float)_rng.NextDouble() * (vc.CentripetalRange[1] - vc.CentripetalRange[0]);
      float t = vc.TangentialRange[0]  + (float)_rng.NextDouble() * (vc.TangentialRange[1]  - vc.TangentialRange[0]);
      return new VortexResponse { CentripetalMult = c, TangentialMult = t };
  }
  ```
  Added `_world.AddComponent(e, SampleVortexResponse(ac))` in `SpawnAsteroid`.
  Added `_world.AddComponent(_player, new VortexResponse { CentripetalMult = pc.VortexCentripetal, TangentialMult = pc.VortexTangential })` in `SpawnPlayer`.
  Added `new VortexResponse { CentripetalMult = 1f, TangentialMult = 1f }` in `SpawnAlien` and `SpawnMothership`.

  ```csharp
  ref var vel = ref world.GetComponent<Velocity>(Player);
  var p = _ctx.Config.Player;
  // Lateral bleed
  Vector2 fwd = aim.Dir; Vector2 rgt = new(fwd.Y, -fwd.X);
  float vAlong = Vector2.Dot(vel.Linear, fwd);
  float vPerp  = Vector2.Dot(vel.Linear, rgt);
  vPerp *= MathF.Exp(-p.LateralDrag * fdt);
  vel.Linear = fwd * vAlong + rgt * vPerp;
  // WASD thrust step toward target
  if (freshPress) vel.Linear += wantDir * p.Impulse;
  float step = p.Thrust * fdt * thrustMult * turboMult * slowBoost;
  Vector2 diff = target - vel.Linear; vel.Linear += ...; // step toward maxSpd
  if (spd > maxSpd) vel.Linear *= maxSpd / spd;
  // Brake on no input
  vel.Linear *= MathF.Exp(-p.BrakeDrag * fdt);
  ```

  **Aim rotation** — rate-limited at `RotSpeed`:

  ```csharp
  float maxTurn = _ctx.Config.Player.RotSpeed * fdt;
  float turn = MathF.Abs(delta) <= maxTurn ? delta : MathF.Sign(delta) * maxTurn;
  aim.Dir = new Vector2(MathF.Cos(currentAngle + turn), MathF.Sin(currentAngle + turn));
  ```
  Then: `t.Rotation = MathF.Atan2(aim.Dir.Y, aim.Dir.X) + MathF.PI * 0.5f;`

  ```csharp
      EnergyScale      = frac.AsteroidEnergyScale,
  };
  Vector2 vRelDir = vRel.LengthSquared() > 1f ? Vector2.Normalize(vRel) : ev.Contact.Normal;
  Vector2 blended = Vector2.Lerp(ev.Contact.Normal, vRelDir, frac.AsteroidDirSpin);
  Vector2 impactDirAB = blended.LengthSquared() > 1e-6f ? Vector2.Normalize(blended) : ev.Contact.Normal;
  ```

- **Duplicate VortexConfig (CS0101)**: Upstream added `VortexConfig` inside `WaveSystemConfig.cs`; our `VortexConfig.cs` was a duplicate. Fixed by deleting `GameEngine/GameConfig/Models/VortexConfig.cs`.

- **CS0136 local variable 'vel' conflict**: The dash skill block declared `ref var vel` inside an `if` block, then the movement block also declared `ref var vel`. C# treats them as same method scope. Fixed by renaming the dash block's variable to `dashVel`.

- **`git add` path error**: Running `git add GameEngine/Assets/...` from wrong directory. Fixed by running from workspace root without the `GameEngine/` prefix.

- **Cannon damage ~187× too weak**: `bulletMass = effectiveEnergy / Max(1, bulletVel²) * 2f` gave `≈0.00107` vs demo's `0.20`. Fixed by using `frac.BulletMass * frac.EnergyScale` directly.

- **Stash pop merge conflicts**: 4 files conflicted after `git stash pop`. Manually resolved all four by merging both sides' additions, then staged with `git add` and dropped stash with `git stash drop`.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 09:18 UTC

All changes build cleanly. Here's a summary of what was fixed:

---

**Bug 1 — Grenade tunneling**: The grenade had no `Collider`, relying only on the raycast (PreviousPosition→Position). When the grenade slows down near its fuse expiry, the per-frame segment becomes tiny (~0.1 px) and can fail to cross an asteroid cell boundary if the grenade is nearly stationary inside one. Fix: gave the grenade a `CircleShape(6f)` collider so `CollisionSystem` detects overlap even when the round is stationary. Added a `GrenadeFuse` check at the top of `OnCollision` (before the FracturableBody guard) to detonate on contact. Added `RemoveComponentImmediate<GrenadeFuse>` as the first act in `OnGrenadeDetonate` to prevent the double-detonation edge case where both the raycast and the collider detect the same grenade in the same frame.

**Bug 2 — Piercing round spin**: `SpawnFracturableBody` sets `AngularDrag = ph.AngularDrag = 0.05f` (very low) for all bodies. After a glancing collision the angular impulse from `CollisionSystem` spins the round up with almost no damping. Fix: overrides `AngularDrag = 4f` on the piercing round's `RigidBody` after spawning.

**Bug 3 — Player abrupt death**: `TransferPlayerToFragment` had a "death condition 2" that triggered game over whenever the cockpit fragment had no cannon/shotgun/propeller/etc cells. Since the cockpit cell's only role is "cockpit", any split that left it isolated instantly killed the player. Fix: removed that condition. The player now only dies when the cockpit cell is directly pulverized (`OnCellPulverized`) or when no cockpit-containing fragment survives a fracture (`if (isPlayer && !cockpitFound)`).

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 09:35 UTC

Let me look at the wave and spawning system in both the game and demo:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 09:36 UTC

Now I have the full picture. Here's the answer:

---

**How waves work in the demo vs the game:**

The **demo** uses a **wave-number** system:
- `_waveNumber` increments each wave; `DefaultBias` gives flat equal weights to all asteroid types from wave 1 onward (ignoring time)
- `WaveDefinition` entries in `game_config.json`'s `waves` array can override this per wave number — but none are defined currently
- Asteroids only: no alien spawning in the demo at all
- Budget starts at 25 (`20 + 1*5`) and grows +5 per wave; cell cap starts at 300 and grows +30 per wave

The **game** uses a **time-based** system driven by `_gameTime` (seconds):
- `spawnBias` entries in `game_config.json` each have `w0/w1/t0/t1` — a lerp from weight `w0` at `t0` seconds to `w1` at `t1` seconds
- Drones appear from t=180s, bruisers from t=420s — so you'd wait 3–7 minutes to see aliens in normal play
- One alien type is sampled per wave; alien count = `budget / baseCost` (capped 1–3)

**Best way to test aliens and later waves in the demo:**

The simplest approach is to add two keys:
- **N** — force the next wave immediately (sets `_waveTimer = 30f` to trigger the threshold, or calls `SpawnNextWave()` directly)
- **Shift+T** (or another key) — advance `_gameTime` forward by +60s, so the time-based bias unlocks later alien types faster

But the demo's wave system is wave-number based and has no alien spawning code. To test aliens specifically, you'd either:

1. **Add a direct alien-spawn shortcut** (e.g. `A` key cycles through alien types and spawns one at the player's position) — quickest to implement
2. **Port the game's time-based wave system to the demo** so `_gameTime` controls the bias and alien sampling matches the game exactly
3. **Edit `game_config.json`**: add explicit `WaveDefinition` entries for specific wave numbers with alien keys in their `Spawns` dictionary — this way wave 1 already has drones and you don't need code changes

**Which is best?** Option 1 (direct spawn shortcut) is fastest for testing specific alien behaviors. Option 3 (config-driven) is zero code but requires understanding the WaveDefinition format. Want me to implement one or both?

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-24 09:42 UTC
