Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:

**Session Part 1 — Bug Fixes (continuation from previous session):**
Four bugs were identified and fixed in `GameEngine/Game/States/PlayingState.cs`:
1. **Grenade tunneling** through asteroids — grenade had no Collider, relied only on raycast; slow movement (~0.1 px/frame near fuse expiry) caused the PreviousPosition→Position segment to never cross an asteroid boundary if the grenade was nearly stationary inside a cell
2. **Piercing round spins too fast** after first collision — all bodies spawned via `SpawnFracturableBody` get `ph.AngularDrag = 0.05f`, which is far too low for a projectile receiving angular impulse from `CollisionSystem`
3. **Player never fractures / dies abruptly** — `TransferPlayerToFragment` had a "death condition 2": if the cockpit-containing fragment had no cells with role "cannon"/"shotgun"/"propeller"/"piercing"/"grenade", game over triggered immediately. Since the cockpit cell's role is "cockpit" (not any functional role), any fracture that left the cockpit isolated caused instant death
4. **Player HUD always shows green** — after fracture, `_player` becomes a new entity with a fresh FractureProcess; the new fragment starts with no pulverized cells, so the HUD always shows green. Determined to be a known limitation of the post-fracture entity transfer design.

**Session Part 2 — Demo Wave System (new feature request):**
User asked for the best way to test aliens and different waves in the demo. After discussion, user confirmed they want:
- Port the game's **time-based wave system** to the demo (replacing demo's current wave-number system)
- **Time controls**: skip forward/backward in game time, force next wave spawn
- **Wave tab redesign**: a game_time slider to derive weights/caps, display derived asteroid+alien bias weights, and a "Spawn" button
- Specifically: "A way to define a specific wave (with all the parameters, game_time to derive weights and caps) in the wave tab and a 'spawn' button could work really well"

---

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- **C# ECS**: `World`, `Entity`, `ISystem`, `EventBus`, fixed timestep 1/120s
- **Deferred entity destruction**: `DestroyEntity` queues work for `FlushDeferred()`. `RemoveComponentImmediate<T>` removes immediately and is safe outside ForEach loops
- **EventBus.Flush()**: uses `while (_queue.TryDequeue(out var item))` — processes events added during flush in the same flush cycle
- **Grenade double-detonation**: Both `RaycastBulletSystem` (via `BulletTag`) and `CollisionSystem` (via new `Collider`) can detect the grenade in the same frame; the first `OnGrenadeDetonate` removes `GrenadeFuse` immediately, the second call finds no `GrenadeFuse` and returns
- **FractureService.BeginFracture**: if `FractureProcess` already exists on an entity, co-propagates (adds another crack front); if budget check fails (`combined < threshold`), absorbs energy without starting a crack
- **TransferPlayerToFragment**: called from `OnFractureCompleted` and `OnFractureSplit` when the cockpit-containing fragment is found; sets `_player = ne`
- **Time-based wave system** (game): `_gameTime` drives everything; `spawnBias` config entries have `w0/w1/t0/t1` for interpolated weights over time; aliens appear when their bias weight > 0 (drones at t0=180s, bruisers at t0=420s)
- **Demo wave-number system** (old): `_waveNumber++` each wave, `DefaultBias()` returns flat weights independent of time, no alien spawning
- **Demo project isolation**: Demo references only engine, SDL platform, GameConfig — NOT the Game project; it defines its own `RaycastBulletSystem`, `BorderDampSystem`, local component structs
- **WaveSystem config**: `BaseBudget`, `BudgetGrowthPerInterval`, `GrowthIntervalSeconds`, `TriggerThreshold`, `GracePeriodSeconds`, `HardTriggerIntervalSeconds`, `BaseCellCap`, `CellCapGrowthAmount`, `MaxCellCap`, `SizeBiasStart`, `SizeBiasEnd`, `SizeBiasRampEnd`, `SpawnBias` dictionary

---

3. Files and Code Sections:

**`GameEngine/Game/States/PlayingState.cs`** — All four bug fixes applied here.

*Fix 1 — OnGrenadeDetonate (around line 891): prevents double-detonation*
```csharp
private void OnGrenadeDetonate(GrenadeDetonateEvent ev)
{
    if (!_world.IsAlive(ev.Grenade)) return;
    if (!_world.HasComponent<GrenadeFuse>(ev.Grenade)) return;  // already detonated this frame
    _world.RemoveComponentImmediate<GrenadeFuse>(ev.Grenade);   // prevent double-detonation
    _world.DestroyEntity(ev.Grenade);
    // ... spawn shrapnel ...
```

*Fix 2 — Grenade spawn (around line 2161): added Collider for CollisionSystem detection*
```csharp
world.AddComponent(b, new RigidBody { Mass = 0.5f, Inertia = 0f, LinearDrag = 1.8f, AngularDrag = 0f, Restitution = 0f, Friction = 0f });
world.AddComponent(b, new Collider { Shape = new CircleShape(6f), Layer = GameLayers.Bullet, Mask = GameLayers.Asteroid | GameLayers.Alien });
world.AddComponent(b, new BulletTag());
world.AddComponent(b, new BulletVisual { Color = new Color(100, 255, 100) });
world.AddComponent(b, new BulletData { WeaponKey = "grenade", Energy = 0f });
world.AddComponent(b, new GrenadeFuse { Remaining = gcfg.FuseTime ?? 1.8f, WeaponKey = "grenade" });
```

*Fix 3 — OnCollision: added grenade check before FracturableBody guard*
```csharp
private void OnCollision(CollisionEvent ev)
{
    Entity eA = ev.EntityA, eB = ev.EntityB;
    if (!_world.IsAlive(eA) || !_world.IsAlive(eB)) return;

    // Grenade detonates on contact — check before FracturableBody guard.
    Entity grEnt = _world.HasComponent<GrenadeFuse>(eA) ? eA
                 : _world.HasComponent<GrenadeFuse>(eB) ? eB
                 : default;
    if (_world.IsAlive(grEnt) && _world.HasComponent<GrenadeFuse>(grEnt))
    {
        var fuse = _world.GetComponent<GrenadeFuse>(grEnt);
        _bus.Publish(new GrenadeDetonateEvent(grEnt, ev.Contact.ContactPoint, fuse.WeaponKey));
        return;
    }

    bool aIsBody = _world.HasComponent<FracturableBody>(eA);
    bool bIsBody = _world.HasComponent<FracturableBody>(eB);
    if (!aIsBody || !bIsBody) return;
    // ... rest of OnCollision
```

*Fix 4 — SpawnPiercingRound: added AngularDrag override after spawning*
```csharp
// High angular drag prevents uncontrolled spin after glancing impacts.
if (_world.HasComponent<RigidBody>(e))
{
    ref var rb = ref _world.GetComponent<RigidBody>(e);
    rb.AngularDrag = 4f;
}
```

*Fix 5 — TransferPlayerToFragment: removed hasFunc death condition*
```csharp
private void TransferPlayerToFragment(Entity ne, in FragmentSpec f,
    AimComponent aim, WeaponCooldowns wc, ActiveWeapon wep, SkillState sk)
{
    _world.AddComponent(ne, new PlayerTag());
    _world.AddComponent(ne, aim);
    _world.AddComponent(ne, wc);
    _world.AddComponent(ne, new ActiveWeapon { Key = wep.Key ?? _ctx.Config.Player.StartingWeapon });
    _world.AddComponent(ne, sk);
    _player = ne;
    // hasFunc death condition removed — player dies only when cockpit is pulverized or gone
}
```

```csharp
public void Flush()
{
    while (_queue.TryDequeue(out var item))
        Dispatch(item.type, item.evt);
}
```
Events published during flush (by handlers) ARE processed in the same flush cycle.

- "Player HUD always green": After each fracture, `_player` becomes a new fragment entity with no pulverized cells. HUD correctly shows the current fragment's state (all green = no damage to THIS fragment yet). Not easily fixable without redesigning the post-fracture entity system.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 11:16 UTC

Let me read the existing materials and material config model to understand the parameter space:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 11:18 UTC

Here's a draft material based on how the fracture engine actually uses each parameter:

```json
"alien_alloy": {
    "toughness": 110,
    "brittleness": 0.08,
    "crackDirectionality": 0.10,
    "grainArea": 5000,
    "minFragmentArea": 800,
    "density": 3.5,
    "kineticFraction": 0.50,
    "surfaceEfficiency": 0.04,
    "spinPreStress": 0.04,
    "crackSpeed": 1,
    "detachCellScale": 0.94,
    "detachCellJitter": 0.005
}
```

---

**`toughness: 110`** (metal = 40)  
The crack threshold is `toughness × struck_cell_mass`. At density 3.5, ship cells are already much heavier than rock cells, so the threshold stacks: a cannon round that shatters a boulder barely dents this. You need either a piercing round held on target or a grenade close-up.

**`density: 3.5`** (metal = 2)  
Mass = density × area. A drone with ~10 cells over ~20 000 px² weighs ~700 000 mass units — roughly 4× a same-sized rock. The collision solver will barely move it on impact, and every energy calculation in the fracture engine multiplies by this mass.

**`brittleness: 0.08`** (metal = 0.15)  
Controls crack transmission: near zero means each crack front dies almost immediately after breaking a bond. You chip one panel loose, not a chain reaction. Also controls scatter randomness of flying fragments — low brittleness means they eject in predictable directions rather than spraying chaotically.

**`crackDirectionality: 0.10`** (metal = 0.15)  
Near-zero means the crack propagates isotropically, spreading damage pressure around the impact point rather than cutting along the bullet vector. The ship absorbs the blow uniformly rather than splitting cleanly.

**`grainArea: 5000`** (metal = 3000)  
Determines how many Voronoi cells are generated: `cellCount ≈ πr²/grainArea`. Fewer, larger structural panels rather than a fine grain. A drone stays at ~6–8 chunks rather than 15+, which is also lighter on the simulation.

**`minFragmentArea: 800`** (metal = 400)  
Any fragment below this area becomes debris dust instead of a physics piece. Large panels don't crumble into micro-shards — a detached piece is always a substantial chunk.

**`surfaceEfficiency: 0.04`** (metal = 0.06)  
After subtracting the threshold energy, only 4% of the remainder actually goes into cracking surface — the rest is absorbed as heat/sound. This is the main reason repeated hits are needed: each round wastes almost all of its energy budget.

**`kineticFraction: 0.50`** (metal = 0.45)  
Of the small energy budget that *does* create fracture, half goes into flinging the detached panel. A piece that finally breaks off punches outward with real force — a reward signal that a hard hit landed.

**`spinPreStress: 0.04`** (metal = 0.08)  
Tangential bonds are weakened proportionally to `ω² × spinPreStress`. Ships rotate slowly and deliberately, so centrifugal pre-cracking should barely apply.

**`crackSpeed: 1`** (metal = 1, ice = 4)  
One bond-break iteration per FractureSimulator step: the fracture unfolds over the maximum number of frames. Combined with low surface efficiency, a hit produces a slow, grinding deformation rather than an instant shatter event.

**`detachCellScale: 0.94, detachCellJitter: 0.005`**  
When a single panel flings free, it shrinks by 6% to show the gap. Near-zero jitter means all panels look the same size — manufactured precision, not natural rock fracture.

---

One thing worth checking in-game: the effective fracture threshold for a drone hit is roughly `110 × (3.5 × cellArea)`. If drones have ~8 cells across a ~15 000 px² shape, each cell ≈ 1 875 px², so threshold ≈ `110 × 3.5 × 1875 ≈ 721 000`. A cannon round delivers around 1–1.5M energy units at full speed, so the first shot *just* breaks the threshold — one chip. Adjust `toughness` up or down by 20–30 to taste once you can spawn a drone in the demo and shoot it.

## 🧑 User · 2026-06-24 12:36 UTC

This session is being continued from a previous conversation that ran out of context. The summary below covers the earlier portion of the conversation.

Summary:
1. Primary Request and Intent:

**Session Part 1 — Demo Wave System (implementation):**
Port the game's time-based wave system to the demo, replacing the demo's wave-number based system. Add:
- Time-parametric spawn weights from `WaveSystem.SpawnBias` (w0→w1 lerp over t0→t1)
- Alien spawning in the demo (drifting FracturableBodies, no AI)
- Keyboard shortcuts: N = force next wave, `[` = -60s game time, `]` = +60s game time
- Wave tab redesign: left panel = session controls (time display, time jumps, force spawn), right panel = wave preview (preview time slider, derived budget/cell cap/size bias, asteroid & alien weight tables, spawn buttons)

**Session Part 2 — Alien Ship Material:**
Draft a "strong ship material" with strong bonds and high density, with explanation of each parameter's physical meaning.

**Session Part 3 — Two Bug Reports:**
1. Save shape (Ctrl+S) doesn't work in the shape editor tab
2. Alien AI is broken: don't move toward player, never fire, don't chase player, too affected by vortex force

---

2. Key Technical Concepts:

- **C# ECS**: `World`, `Entity`, `ISystem`, `EventBus`, fixed timestep 1/120s, `ForEach`, `FlushDeferred`
- **SpawnBiasEntry**: Time-parametric weights: `w = W0 + (t-T0)/(T1-T0) * (W1-W0)` clamped to [W0,W1]
- **WaveSystemConfig**: `BaseBudget + intervals * BudgetGrowthPerInterval`, `TriggerThreshold`, `GracePeriodSeconds`, `HardTriggerIntervalSeconds`, `SpawnDelaySeconds`, `SizeBiasStart/End/RampEnd`
- **SDL Key Mapping**: `MapKey` in `SdlGameWindow.cs` translates SDL syms to `KeyCode`; Control key (1073741724, 1073741728) was missing from the switch
- **PhysicsSystem.ApplyForce**: Accumulates force, applies as `dvLin = (AccumulatedForce / Mass) * dt` per step — this is force-based (Newtons)
- **Player thrust model**: Direct velocity model (px/s change per frame), NOT force-based — incompatible scale with alien thrust config
- **AliveWeaponFraction vs AlivePropellerFraction asymmetry**: Weapon returns 0 for no cells (blocks firing); Propeller correctly returns 1 for no cells (full thrust)
- **Terminal velocity**: `v_t = thrust / (mass * linearDrag)` — with titanium density 3.5, area ~12100, mass ~42350, terminal vel = 680 / (42350 × 0.05) ≈ 0.32 px/s — aliens are essentially immobile from thrust
- **VortexSystem**: Applies centripetal + tangential force proportional to distance from center × CentripetalMult/TangentialMult; cap = force × capFrames (100 per config)
- **Context steering (DroneSteering)**: 8-direction interest/danger maps; interest toward player (weight=pursuit=0.8), danger away from asteroids and boundaries (avoidance=1.0, separation=1.2)
- **Layers**: Asteroid=1, Player=2, Ghost=4, Alien=8 (newly added)
- **Material parameters**: toughness (bond threshold), brittleness (crack propagation + scatter), crackDirectionality (impact vs isotropic), grainArea (cell count), minFragmentArea (debris threshold), density (mass), kineticFraction (fragment velocity share), surfaceEfficiency (energy→crack surface), spinPreStress (centrifugal weakening), crackSpeed (propagation speed), detachCellScale/Jitter

- **New `SpawnNextWave()`**:
```csharp
private void SpawnNextWave()
{
    _waveNumber++;
    var ws = _gc.WaveSystem;
    float gInterval = MathF.Max(1f, ws.GrowthIntervalSeconds);
    int intervals   = (int)(_gameTime / gInterval);
    int budget      = ws.BaseBudget + intervals * ws.BudgetGrowthPerInterval;
    _maxLiveCells   = Math.Min(ws.BaseCellCap + intervals * ws.CellCapGrowthAmount, ws.MaxCellCap);
    float rampT   = ws.SizeBiasRampEnd > 0f ? MathF.Min(1f, _gameTime / ws.SizeBiasRampEnd) : 1f;
    float sizeBias = ws.SizeBiasStart + rampT * (ws.SizeBiasEnd - ws.SizeBiasStart);
    var asteroidBias = new Dictionary<string, float>();
    var alienBias    = new Dictionary<string, float>();
    foreach (var (key, entry) in ws.SpawnBias)
    {
        float w = EvalSpawnWeight(entry, _gameTime);
        if (w <= 0f) continue;
        if (_gc.Asteroids.ContainsKey(key))     asteroidBias[key] = w;
        else if (_gc.Entities.ContainsKey(key)) alienBias[key]    = w;
    }
    // [asteroid spawning, alien sampling/spawning, LogAndBannerWave]
}
```
- **New `EvalSpawnWeight()`**:
```csharp
private static float EvalSpawnWeight(SpawnBiasEntry e, float t)
{
    if (t <= e.T0) return e.W0;
    if (t >= e.T1) return e.W1;
    float f = (t - e.T0) / (e.T1 - e.T0);
    return e.W0 + f * (e.W1 - e.W0);
}
```
- **New `SpawnAlien()`**: Builds FracturableBody from ec.Shape, spawns with `AsteroidColor { Fill = new Color(80, 50, 120), Outline = new Color(160, 100, 220) }`, then overrides collider `Layer = Layers.Alien`, `Mask = Layers.Asteroid | Layers.Player | Layers.Alien`, adds `AlienTag` and `AlienVariant { Key = typeKey }`
- **Updated `LogAndBannerWave()`**: Signature changed to `(List<(string,float)> spawns, List<string> alienSpawns, int budget, float sizeBias)`. Banner line 1: `$"WAVE {_waveNumber}   T={_gameTime:0.0}s"`
- **New public API on DemoSession**:
```csharp
public float GameTime { get => _gameTime; set => _gameTime = MathF.Max(0f, value); }
public void ForceNextWave()
{
    _pendingWave = false;
    SpawnNextWave();
    _waveTimer = 0f;
}
```

```csharp
private static float EvalBias(SpawnBiasEntry e, float t)
{
    if (t <= e.T0) return e.W0;
    if (t >= e.T1) return e.W1;
    float f = (t - e.T0) / (e.T1 - e.T0);
    return e.W0 + f * (e.W1 - e.W0);

```

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 12:39 UTC

Clean build. All four fixes are in:

1. **Ctrl+S save shape** — `SdlGameWindow.MapKey` now maps SDL syms `1073741724` (LCTRL) and `1073741728` (RCTRL) to `EngineKey.Control`.

2. **Aliens never fire** — `AliveWeaponFraction` returns `1f` when the body has no weapon-tagged cells (matching the pattern in `AlivePropellerFraction`). Ships without dedicated cannon cells can always fire.

3. **Aliens don't move** — Thrust now uses the same direct velocity model as the player (`vel += step * toward_desired_velocity`) instead of `PhysicsSystem.ApplyForce`. With titanium mass ~42350, the Newtonian model was giving 0.0001 px/s per step; the velocity model gives `cfg.Thrust / 120 = 5.67 px/s` per step and reaches `cfg.Speed = 220 px/s` in ~0.3 seconds.

4. **Vortex too strong** — `VortexResponse` for drones/bruisers is now `{CentripetalMult = 0.15f, TangentialMult = 0.08f}`. VortexSystem applies velocity changes directly (bypassing mass), so at full strength the vortex could cap centripetal velocity at 83 px/s — more than a third of the alien's flight speed. At 0.15×, the cap drops to ~12 px/s which the thrust model trivially counteracts.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 14:34 UTC

Let me look at how `FractureService.BeginFracture` uses the mass parameter to understand the damage model:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 14:36 UTC

The `energy` field in weapon config is never actually passed to `FractureService` — fracture energy is computed purely from `bulletMass * bulletVel²` where `bulletMass` is a fixed global constant. Lowering `energy` does nothing. The fix: for alien bullets, scale `bulletMass` by `weaponEnergy / referenceEnergy` so the config field directly drives damage.

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 14:36 UTC

Same fix for the demo's `OnBulletHit`:

## 🤖 Claude · 2026-06-24 14:36 UTC

The root cause: `bulletMass` is a global constant (`BulletMass × EnergyScale = 0.20`), and fracture energy = `½ × bulletMass × velocity²`. The `energy` field in weapon config was stored in `BulletData` but never passed into the fracture calculation.

**The fix**: for alien bullets (`AlienBulletTag`), `bulletMass` is scaled by `weaponEnergy / referenceEnergy` where the reference is the player's starting weapon (cannon at 1200). So:

- `cannon_alien` with `energy: 12` → scale = 12/1200 = **1%** of cannon damage  
- `cannon_alien` with `energy: 400` → **33%** of cannon damage
- `cannon_alien` with `energy: 1200` → **100%** of cannon damage (same as player cannon)

Player weapon damage is unchanged — the scaling only applies when `AlienBulletTag` is present. Start with `energy` around 300–600 for alien cannons that do real but non-lethal damage.
